The Soul Cannot Cease: Refuting the First Possibility via an Opposite
Three arguments refuting soul's annihilation by a new opposite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the rational soul cannot be destroyed by the existence of an opposite, based on three logical arguments.

Core Idea
The soul is indestructible because no opposite can overpower it.

This lesson continues the proof of the soul's immortality by examining one specific way it might cease: through the emergence of an opposite. The author presents three decisive reasons showing this scenario is impossible, relying on principles of opposition, strength, and empirical observation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Notice the logical structure: an exhaustive division followed by a focused refutation.
The passage is dense; take time to absorb the flow.
2
Identify the exhaustive division
The author sets up two possibilities for the soul's cessation: either due to the existence of something it needed to lack, or the absence of something it needed to have. Recognize why the first possibility is selected for detailed refutation.
The second possibility is not elaborated here; it is refuted elsewhere.
3
Analyze each of the three reasons
The author gives three reasons why the first possibility is impossible: (1) Opposition is mutual, so repelling is easier; (2) Circularity arises if we attribute removal to a new opposite; (3) The supposed opposite can only be accident, body, or non-material substance—each is shown incapable.
Pay special attention to the third reason, which uses induction to show souls do not oppose each other.
4
Reflect on the use of induction
The author uses complete induction (استقراء تام) as evidence that souls are not mutually repelling. Consider why this empirical observation is considered convincing in this rational argument.
Induction here provides predominant conjecture (ظن غالب) not absolute certainty, but suffices to refute the possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية في بيان أن النفس الناطقة لا تقبل الفساد : إنها لو عدمت بعد وجودها، لكان عدمها لا بد وأن يكون، إما لوجود شيء، كانت النفس محتاجة إلى عدمه، أو لعدم شيء كانت النفس محتاجة إلى وجوده . والقسمان باطلان، فبطل القول بعدمها. أما الحصر فظاهر، وأما بيان فساد القسم الأول وهو أن النفس تعدم لوجود شيء كانت النفس محتاجة إلى عدمه . فهو أن نقول : إن ذلك الشيء يجب أن يكون ضـداً لجـوهـر النفس، ويجب أن يقال : إن ذلك الضد ما كان موجوداً حال بقاء النفس، وإنما حدث بعد ذلك . وهو محال لوجوه : الأول : إن المضادة حاصلة من الجانبين، فلم يكن فناء النفس لأجل حدوث ذلك الضد، أولى من اندفاع ذلك الضد، لأجل قيام النفس، بل هذا الثاني أولى لما قيل : إن الدفع أسهل من الرفع . والثاني : إن طريان ذلك الضد الأول . فلو عللنا زوال الضد الأول، بطريان الثاني . لزم الدور . والثالث : إن الذي يفرض مضاداً لوجود هذه النفس إما أن يكون عرضاً أو متحيزاً ، أو جوهر مجرداً. والأولان باطلان . لأنا بينا : أن العرض والجسم أضعف حالاً من الجوهر المجرد، والأضعف لا يقوى على إعدام الأقوى، ولأن الأجسام والأعراض موجودة مع هذه النفوس الحاضرة . وذلك يدل على انتفاء المضادة بينها وبين النفوس . والثالث أيضاً محال . لأنا إن قلنا : النفوس الناطقة متماثلة ، فقد زال هذا الخيال، لأن المضادة والمعاندة لا تحصل إلا عند اختلاف الطبائع والماهيات . وإن قلنا : إنها مختلفة في الماهيات . فالمضادة أيضاً غير حاصلة . لأنا نعلم بالضرورة : أن جواهر النفوس غـيـر متدافعة ولا متمانعة، بدليل : الاستقراء التام . فإن نفوس الناس الحاضرين لا يضاد بعضها بعضاً . والاستقراء يفيد الظن الغالب
The second proof in clarifying that the rational soul does not accept corruption: If it were to cease after its existence, its non-existence would necessarily have to be either due to the existence of something which the soul needed to lack, or due to the absence of something which the soul needed to have. Both divisions are false, so the statement of its cessation is false. As for the exhaustive division, it is apparent. As for clarifying the corruption of the first division, which is that the soul ceases to exist due to the existence of something which the soul needed to lack, then it is that we say: That thing must be an opposite (ضد) to the substance of the soul, and it must be said that that opposite was not existing at the time of the soul's persistence, but rather originated after that. That is impossible for reasons: First: Opposition is from both sides, so the annihilation of the soul due to the occurrence of that opposite is not more likely than the repulsion of that opposite due to the soul's persistence; rather this second is more likely because it is said that repelling is easier than removing. Second: The occurrence of that first opposite. So if we attribute the removal of the first opposite to the occurrence of the second, circularity (دور) would follow. Third: That which is supposed as opposed to the existence of this soul is either an accident (عرض) or a body (متحيز) or a non-material substance (جوهر مجرد). The first two are false: because we have shown that the accident and the body are weaker in state than the non-material substance, and the weaker has no power to annihilate the stronger, and because bodies and accidents exist together with these present souls, and that indicates the absence of opposition between them and the souls. The third is also impossible: because if we say the rational souls are similar, then this notion disappears, because opposition and contrariety only occur with difference of natures and quiddities. And if we say that they differ in quiddities, then opposition is also not obtained, because we know necessarily that the substances of souls are not mutually repelling nor mutually inhibiting, by evidence of complete induction (استقراء تام). Indeed, the souls of present people do not oppose one another. And induction provides predominant conjecture.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a structured proof (الحجة الثانية) showing the rational soul's immortality. It begins by setting up an exhaustive disjunction: if the soul could cease, it would be either because something it needed to be absent came into existence, or because something it needed to be present ceased. Both are refuted. The author then focuses on the first division. If the soul were destroyed by something coming into existence, that thing must be an opposite (ضد) of the soul's substance, and it must have originated after the soul. This is impossible for three reasons: (1) Opposition is mutual (من الجانبين). If a new opposite appears, it is just as likely that the soul repels it as that it destroys the soul; indeed repelling is easier (الدفع أسهل من الرفع). (2) If we try to explain the removal of a previous opposite by the new one, circularity results. (3) The supposed opposite can only be an accident, a body, or a non-material substance. Accidents and bodies are weaker than the non-material soul, so cannot destroy it; moreover bodies and accidents coexist with souls without opposition. A non-material substance (another soul) cannot be an opposite either because all souls are either similar (so no difference to generate opposition) or different (but empirical observation—complete induction—shows that souls do not oppose each other). Therefore, the first division is impossible.

Key Terms
ضد (opposite)
دور (circularity)
عرض (accident)
متحيز (body)
جوهر مجرد (non-material substance)
استقراء تام (complete induction)
مضادة (opposition)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul could be destroyed by a strong external force, such as a powerful body or accident.
Correction: The author argues that bodies and accidents are weaker than the non-material soul, so they cannot annihilate it. Moreover, they coexist with souls without opposition, showing they are not true opposites.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the 'third reason' in refuting the first division?
A) The soul is stronger than any accident or body, and no other soul can oppose it.
B) The soul can only be destroyed by a material opposite.
C) The soul is subject to decay like bodies.
D) Induction proves that souls do not exist.

Key Takeaway
The soul cannot be annihilated by the emergence of an opposite, because such an opposite would either be too weak or cannot truly oppose a non-material substance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Since your soul is indestructible and will face eternal consequences, what single habit are you willing to change today to ensure that your soul is not heading toward ruin?
?
The author argues that no external force can overpower the soul. Yet you allow internal weaknesses like pride and negligence to weaken your relationship with Allah. What specific internal enemy will you confront this week, and what action will you take to fortify your soul against it?
?
If complete induction shows that souls do not oppose each other, why do you sometimes feel threatened by others' existence or success? How can you truly internalize that no human soul can harm you except by Allah's decree, and what change in your interactions would that produce?

Refutation of the Second Possibility: Permanent Causes
The author refutes the idea that souls end due to loss of causes, but leaves a temporal condition objection unanswered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the soul cannot cease to exist due to the absence of its causes, given that those causes are eternal non-material entities, and you will recognize the remaining objection about temporal conditions that this passage leaves unanswered.

Core Idea
The soul's causes are eternal; they cannot perish, so the soul cannot perish by their absence.

In this passage, the author tackles the second possibility for the soul's annihilation: that it ceases because something it needed is no longer present. He argues that the efficient causes of the soul and its cognitions are eternal non-material entities that do not pass away. However, he then presents an objection: perhaps the soul depends not on the cause itself but on a temporal condition. This objection is not answered in this passage, leaving the argument incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's use of 'amā' and 'fa' to structure the argument.
2
Identify the second division
The author is refuting the second possibility: that the soul ceases due to the absence of something it needed. Understand what this possibility claims.
3
Examine the proof
The author says the efficient causes of the soul and its cognitions are eternal non-material entities. How does this refute the possibility?
Consider why the eternity of causes prevents the soul from ceasing due to their absence.
4
Notice the objection
The passage ends with an objection: the soul's existence might depend on a temporal condition. When that condition disappears, the soul disappears. This is presented as the only remaining possibility.
The passage does not refute this objection; it may be continued later.
5
Reflect on the incompleteness
Why might the author have ended here? What might come next in the argument? Consider the implications for the overall proof of immortality.
This lesson serves as a moment to recognize a gap in the reasoning as presented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان فساد القسم الثاني : وهو القول بأن هذه النفوس عدمت لعدم شيء كانت النفوس محتاجة إليه . فهو أنا سنقيم الدلالة على أن العلل الموجدة لجواهر النفوس : موجودات مجردة دائمة مبرأة عن الحدوث والزوال. وكذلك العلل الموجدة للمعارف الحاصلة في جواهر النفوس : موجودات مجردة مصونة عن الفناء والزوال. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع أن يقال : إن هذه النفوس تعدم بعدم عللها . فلم يبق إلا أن يقال : إنه لا شك أن تأثير تلك العلل في وجود هذه النفوس الحادثة قد كان موقوفاً على شرط حادث ، وإلا لدام المعلول بدوام العلة ، فزالت هذه النفوس لزوال تلك الشرائط .
As for clarifying the corruption of the second division, which is the statement that these souls cease to exist due to the absence of something which the souls needed to have: We will establish the proof that the efficient causes of the substances of souls are non-material existents, perpetual, free from origination and passing away. Similarly, the efficient causes of the cognitions (معارف) present in the substances of souls are non-material existents, immune from annihilation and passing away. If it is so, it is impossible to say that these souls cease to exist due to the absence of their causes. So nothing remains except to say: 'Undoubtedly, the effect of those causes on the existence of these originated souls had been dependent on a temporal condition; otherwise the effect would have persisted with the persistence of the cause. So these souls disappeared due to the disappearance of those conditions.'
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents the refutation of the second division: the soul might cease because something it needed to have is no longer present. The author argues that the causes that bring the soul into existence (العلل الموجدة لجواهر النفوس) and the causes of its cognitions are eternal non-material entities (موجودات مجردة دائمة). Since they are permanent, the soul cannot cease due to their absence. However, the passage then presents a possible objection: the soul's existence may depend on a temporal condition (شرط حادث) rather than the cause itself, so when that condition disappears, the soul also disappears. The text ends here without explicitly refuting this objection, suggesting the section may be incomplete or the refutation is implied. This lesson ends with an unresolved point, marking it for further review.

Key Terms
علل موجدة (efficient causes)
موجودات مجردة (non-material existents)
شرط حادث (temporal condition)
معارف (cognitions)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul could cease to exist if something it needs (like a cause) is absent.
Correction: The author argues that the efficient causes of the soul and its cognitions are eternal non-material entities that do not perish, so they cannot be absent.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the soul cannot cease due to the absence of its causes?
A) Because the causes are stronger than the soul.
B) Because the causes are eternal non-material entities that do not perish.
C) Because the soul creates its own causes.
D) Because the causes are accidents that depend on the soul.

Key Takeaway
The soul cannot cease to exist due to the absence of its causes because those causes are eternal non-material entities; however, the passage leaves unresolved the objection that the soul might depend on a temporal condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may think that your soul's well-being depends on certain conditions—health, wealth, relationships. But if these are merely temporal conditions, what happens when they fail? This lesson challenges you to reconsider: is your soul's ultimate security found in the Eternal or in fleeting circumstances? Identify one condition you treat as essential and surrender it to the Eternal today.
?
The author establishes that the soul's causes are eternal, yet he does not dismiss the possibility of a temporal condition. In your life, is your connection to your Creator conditioned by something temporary (like Ramadan, a prayer routine, a spiritual high)? What would it mean to make that connection unconditional?
?
If the soul is not destroyed by the absence of its causes, then what truly threatens your soul? The lesson invites you to examine whether you fear losing things that are not your soul's real causes. Name one such fear and consciously entrust it to the Eternal.

Refutation of Annihilation by a Contrary
Refutes the claim that souls can be annihilated by a contrary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational souls cannot be annihilated by any contrary—whether accident, body, or another immaterial substance.

Core Idea
No contrary can destroy a rational soul, whether physical or spiritual.

This passage systematically refutes the notion that rational souls can be destroyed by a contrary. It examines every possible type of contrary—accidents, bodies, and other immaterial substances—and demonstrates that none can cause annihilation. The argument is built on the nature of substances and observed coexistence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the logical flow: a preliminary argument about circularity, then a classification of possible contraries, followed by refutations.
The passage uses technical terms like 'جوهر مجرد' (immaterial substance).
2
Identify the three types of contraries
The passage lists three possibilities for what could be a contrary to the soul: an accident, a body, or an immaterial substance. Recognize how each is defined.
These three categories exhaust the types of created entities.
3
Understand why accidents and bodies fail
The passage gives two reasons: accidents and bodies are weaker than the immaterial soul, and they are observed to coexist with souls, showing no contrariety.
Coexistence is key: if they were truly contrary, they could not coexist.
4
Understand why another immaterial substance fails
Even if the contrary is another immaterial substance, it cannot annihilate the soul. Whether souls are similar or different in essence, contrariety is impossible: similar souls cannot oppose; different souls are observed not to oppose (by induction).
Induction from present souls shows no mutual opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني أولى لما قيل : إن الدفع أسهل من الرفع . والثاني : إن طريان ذلك الضد الأول . فلو عللنا زوال الضد الأول ، بطريان الثاني . لزم الدور . والثالث : إن الذي يفرض مضاداً لوجود هذه النفس إما أن يكون عرضاً أو متحيزاً ، أو جوهر مجرداً. والأولان باطلان . لأنا بينا : أن العرض والجسم أضعف حالاً من الجوهر المجرد ، والأضعف لا يقوى على إعدام الأقوى ، ولأن الأجسام والأعراض موجودة مع هذه النفوس الحاضرة . وذلك يدل على انتفاء المضادة بينها وبين النفوس . والثالث أيضاً محال . لأنا إن قلنا : النفوس الناطقة متماثلة ، فقد زال هذا الخيال ، لأن المضادة والمعاندة لا تحصل إلا عند اختلاف الطبائع والماهيات . وإن قلنا : إنها مختلفة في الماهيات . فالمضادة أيضاً غير حاصلة . لأنا نعلم بالضرورة : أن جواهر النفوس غير متدافعة ولا متمانعة ، بدليل : الاستقراء التام . فإن نفوس الناس الحاضرين لا يضاد بعضها بعضاً . والاستقراء يفيد الظن الغالب
The second is more appropriate because it was said: 'Repelling is easier than removing.' And the second: that the occurrence of that first opposite [is considered]. For if we attribute the removal of the first opposite to the occurrence of the second, a circularity would follow. And the third: that what is supposed to be contrary to the existence of this soul is either an accident, or a body, or an immaterial substance. The first two are false. Because we have shown that the accident and the body are weaker in condition than the immaterial substance, and the weaker cannot overpower the stronger to annihilate it, and because bodies and accidents exist alongside these present souls. That indicates the absence of contrariety between them and the souls. The third is also impossible. For if we say: the rational souls are similar, this illusion is removed, because contrariety and opposition only occur with difference in natures and essences. And if we say: they are different in essences, then contrariety is still not obtained. Because we know by necessity that the substances of souls are not mutually repelling nor mutually opposing, as evidenced by complete induction. For the souls of present people do not oppose one another. And induction yields predominant conjecture.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage refutes the claim that rational souls can be annihilated by a contrary. It begins by presenting an argument that if we use the occurrence of a second contrary to explain the removal of the first, we fall into circular reasoning. Then it classifies possible contraries of the soul into three kinds: an accident, a body, or an immaterial substance. The first two (accident and body) are shown to be impossible because they are weaker than the soul and are observed to coexist with souls in the present world, proving no contrariety. The third (an immaterial substance) is also impossible: if all souls are similar in essence, no contrariety can exist; if they differ, we still observe through complete induction that souls do not oppose each other (e.g., souls of people present do not conflict). Induction yields strong probability. Thus the soul cannot be destroyed by any contrary.

Key Terms
النفوس الناطقة
المضادة
جوهر مجرد
عرض
جسم
الاستقراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A contrary, such as a physical force or another spiritual entity, can destroy or annihilate a rational soul.
Correction: No type of contrary—accident, body, or immaterial substance—can annihilate a rational soul. Accidents and bodies are weaker and coexist; immaterial souls are observed not to oppose each other.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it impossible for a body or an accident to annihilate a rational soul?
A) Because bodies and accidents are weaker than the immaterial soul.
B) Because bodies and accidents are stronger than the soul.
C) Because the soul is an accident itself.
D) Because bodies and accidents do not exist alongside souls.

Key Takeaway
A rational soul cannot be annihilated by any contrary because accidents, bodies, and other immaterial substances all fail to oppose it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever acted as if your soul could be harmed or destroyed by worldly influences (like wealth, status, or physical pain)? What does this lesson teach you about the true nature of your soul's invulnerability? How must your priorities change in light of this truth?
?
The passage argues that souls do not oppose each other. Think of a person with whom you have conflict. Is it possible that the conflict exists only at the level of bodies or accidents (words, actions), not at the level of souls? How can this realization transform how you relate to them from now on?
?
If no contrary can annihilate your rational soul, then what is the only thing that can separate you from your Creator? Does your daily life reflect a belief that the soul is imperishable, or do you live as if this world is all there is? What one change will you make today to align your actions with this truth?

Refutation of Annihilation Due to Cessation of Conditions
Refutes the second argument for soul annihilation: cessation of conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the cessation of conditions cannot cause the annihilation of rational souls, as argued by Imam ar-Razi in Al-Matalib al-Aliyah.

Core Idea
Perpetual souls cannot depend on temporary conditions.

Imam ar-Razi continues his refutation of soul annihilation by tackling the second argument: that souls cease because the conditions on which they depend cease. He first establishes that the causes of souls are eternal, and then shows that any temporary condition is incompatible with the soul's perpetual nature. This passage is a masterclass in logical reasoning about immaterial existents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Get a feel for the argument's flow without trying to analyze every detail.
Notice the clear structure: first a premise, then a conditional objection, then a refutation.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two parts: first, establishing that the causes of souls are eternal, so souls cannot be annihilated by their causes ceasing. Second, addressing the claim that the soul depends on a temporary condition that ceased.
The word 'فلم يبق إلا أن يقال' signals the transition to the condition argument.
3
Analyze the condition argument's refutation
The author divides the condition into two possibilities: either it is eternal (permanent) or not. For each, he shows impossibility. Map out this division mentally.
Use the guided_breakdown below to follow the logical steps.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by asserting that rational souls are not susceptible to non-existence or corruption. Consider why this conclusion is important for the overall argument about the soul's survival after death.
This relates to the broader Islamic theological claim about the immortality of the soul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان فساد القسم الثاني : وهو القول بأن هذه النفوس عدمت لعدم شيء كانت النفوس محتاجة إليه . فهو أنا سنقيم الدلالة على أن العلل الموجدة لجواهر النفوس : موجودات مجردة دائمة مبرأة عن الحدوث والزوال. وكذلك العلل الموجدة للمعارف الحاصلة في جواهر النفوس : موجودات مجردة مصونة عن الفناء والزوال. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع أن يقال : إن هذه النفوس تعدم بعدم عللها . فلم يبق إلا أن يقال : إنه لا شك أن تأثير تلك العلل في وجود هذه النفوس الحادثة قد كان موقوفاً على شرط حادث ، وإلا لدام المعلول بدوام العلة ، فزالت هذه النفوس ، لزوال تلك الشرائط . فنقول : هذا أيضاً باطل . لأن تلك الشرائط، إما أن تكون باقية ، وإما أن لا تكون باقية . فإن كانت باقية عاد التقسيم المذكور في كيفية عدمها بعد بقائها . وإن لم تكن باقية امتنع كونها شرائط لوجود النفوس . لأن النفوس باقية وتلك الأشياء غير باقية . وكون الباقي مشروط الوجود بما لا يبقى : محال . فثبت بهذا البيان والتقرير : أن النفوس الناطقة غير قابلة للعدم والفساد . وهو المطلوب
As for the demonstration of the invalidity of the second division—namely, the statement that these souls ceased to exist due to the non-existence of something on which the souls were dependent—it is that we will establish the proof that the causes that bring the substances of souls into existence are immaterial existents, perpetual, free from origination and passing away. Likewise, the causes that bring the cognitions subsisting in the substances of souls into existence are immaterial existents, guarded against annihilation and passing away. And if this is the case, it is impossible to say that these souls cease to exist with the non-existence of their causes. So nothing remains except to say that there is no doubt that the influence of those causes in the existence of these originated souls was dependent upon a condition that had come into being, otherwise the effect would have continued with the continuance of the cause, and thus these souls ceased due to the cessation of those conditions. Then we say: this too is invalid. Because those conditions are either perpetual or not perpetual. If they are perpetual, the division mentioned concerning the manner of their non-existence after their permanence returns. And if they are not perpetual, it is impossible for them to be conditions for the existence of the souls, because the souls are perpetual while those things are not perpetual. And the existence of something perpetual being conditioned by that which does not endure is impossible. So by this explanation and exposition, it is established that rational souls are not susceptible to non-existence and corruption. That is what was sought.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage refutes the second argument that souls are annihilated because the conditions on which they depend cease. The author first establishes that the causes of souls are eternal immaterial beings, so they cannot cease. The only possible claim left is that the effect (the soul) depended on a temporary condition that ceased. The author then shows this is invalid: the condition must be either permanent or impermanent. If permanent, the same problem of explaining how it ceased arises. If impermanent, it cannot be a condition for something that is perpetual (the soul), because it is impossible for a perpetual thing to have its existence conditioned by something that does not endure. Therefore the souls are not subject to annihilation.

Key Terms
علل
شرائط
مجرد
جوهر النفس
معلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A soul can be annihilated if a condition on which its existence depends ceases.
Correction: The soul is a perpetual entity; its existence cannot be conditioned by something temporary. Even if a condition ceased, the soul, being permanent, cannot depend on it. Therefore, the cessation of a condition does not entail the soul's annihilation.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that conditions for the soul's existence cannot be impermanent?
A) Because the soul is impermanent itself.
B) Because the causes of the soul are eternal, so conditions must be eternal.
C) Because the soul is perpetual, and it is impossible for a perpetual thing to be conditioned by something that does not endure.
D) Because the conditions are always perpetual.

Key Takeaway
Rational souls are perpetual and cannot be annihilated by the cessation of any condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author argues that a perpetual soul cannot depend on temporary conditions. What temporary conditions in your life—such as health, relationships, or status—do you unconsciously treat as essential to your identity and happiness? How would your life change if you truly lived as though your soul's existence depends only on the Eternal?
?
This proof shows that the soul is not subject to corruption. If you truly believed this with certainty, how would it change the way you face your own death or the death of loved ones? What concrete thought or action could you adopt today to live in light of this truth?

Objection and Answer on the Soul's Annihilability
Objection and answer on the soul's possible annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that the soul's originatedness implies its possible annihilation is refuted by distinguishing between the possibility of origination and the possibility of corruption after existence.

Core Idea
The possibility of coming into existence is not the same as the possibility of ceasing to exist.

This passage presents a sophisticated objection against the soul's immortality and its answer. The objectors argue that if the soul is created, it must be capable of non-existence. The response cuts through the argument by noting that the premise itself is disputed and that a crucial distinction has already been made between the possibility of origination and the possibility of corruption after existence. Let's examine the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the objection as presented: the soul is originated, therefore it must be capable of non-existence. Notice how this initial claim is argued.
2
Identify the two branches of the dilemma
The objection considers two cases for the capacity for non-existence: either it is an essential concomitant or an accidental attribute. Trace each branch and its consequence.
The first branch leads to necessary capability of corruption; the second leads to an infinite regress.
3
Analyze the answer's structure
The answer gives two points: first, the premise that souls are originated is not established; second, a distinction between two kinds of possibility has already been made. Understand why these points dismiss the objection.
4
Grasp the key distinction
Focus on the distinction between imkan al-huduth (possibility of origination) and imkan al-fasad (possibility of corruption). The objection conflates them; the answer separates them.
This is the central insight that refutes the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج القائلون بأنها قابلة للفساد : بأن قالوا : ثبت أنها حادثة ، كونها قابلة للعدم . فقابلية العدم، إن كانت من اللوازم ، وجب بقاؤها أبداً فوجب كونها قابلة للعدم بعد وجودها . فتكون قابلة للفساد . وإن لم تكن تلك القابلية من لوازم تلك الماهيات كانت صفة عارضة لها . فقابلية تلك القابلية ، إن كانت من اللوازم عاد الإلزام ، وإن لم تكن من اللوازم كانت مسبوقة بقابلية أخرى إلى غير النهاية . وهو محال . والجواب : هذا الكلام بناء على أن النفوس حادثة ، والبحث فيه ما تقدم . ثم نقول : الفرق بين إمكان الحدوث وبين إمكان الفساد بعد الوجود : قد ذكرناه . فلا فائدة في الإعادة والله أعلم
And those who say that [souls] are susceptible to corruption argued by saying: it has been established that they are originated, so they must be capable of non-existence. So the capacity for non-existence, if it is among the necessary concomitants, then their permanence forever would be necessary, and thus they must be capable of non-existence after their existence. So they would be susceptible to corruption. And if that capacity is not among the necessary concomitants of those essences, it would be an accidental attribute to them. Then the capacity for that capacity, if it is among the necessary concomitants, the same necessary consequence returns; and if it is not among the necessary concomitants, it would be preceded by another capacity ad infinitum, which is impossible. The answer: this statement is based on the premise that souls are originated, and the investigation into that has preceded. Then we say: the distinction between the possibility of origination and the possibility of corruption after existence has already been mentioned by us. So there is no benefit in repeating. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the immortality of the soul and replies to it. The objectors argue that since the soul is originated (haditha), it must have a capacity for non-existence. They then analyze this capacity: if it is an essential necessary concomitant of the soul, then the soul would necessarily always have it, implying it can cease; if it is accidental, then the capacity itself needs another capacity, leading to either a regress or the same problem. The answer first notes that the whole objection rests on the premise that souls are originated, which has already been discussed (and presumably refuted) earlier. Additionally, the author states that a distinction has already been made between the possibility of origination (imkan al-huduth) and the possibility of corruption after existence (imkan al-fasad ba'd al-wujud), so there is no need to repeat it. Thus the objection is dismissed.

Key Terms

لوازم
عارضة
إمكان الحدوث
إمكان الفساد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if something is possible to come into existence, it is also possible to cease to exist.
Correction: The possibility of origination (imkan al-huduth) and the possibility of corruption after existence (imkan al-fasad) are distinct. Something can be originated without necessarily being capable of annihilation.

Checkpoint
What is the key distinction the answer relies on to refute the objection?
A) The distinction between essential and accidental attributes.
B) The distinction between the possibility of origination and the possibility of corruption after existence.
C) The distinction between the soul and the body.
D) The distinction between necessary and contingent.

Key Takeaway
The objection that the soul's createdness implies its annihilation fails because the possibility of origination is distinct from the possibility of corruption after existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the possibility of being created does not automatically mean you can cease to exist. Your soul, once brought into being, may be permanent by God's decree. Yet how often do you live as if this life is all there is—chasing fleeting pleasures and ignoring the eternal accountability that awaits your immortal soul? What one change will you make today to live in light of your soul’s permanence?
?

But the response separates the capacity for coming into existence from the capacity for passing away. One Soul in Two Bodies or Two Souls in One Body?
The author argues for the logical possibility of one soul in two bodies and two souls in one body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dialectical arguments for the logical possibility of one soul managing two bodies and two souls managing one body.

Core Idea
The soul-body relationship allows for logical possibilities beyond ordinary experience.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah explores two intriguing questions: can one soul manage two bodies, or can two souls manage one body? The author presents arguments for both possibilities, showing that they are not absurd from a rational perspective. As we read it, we will examine the reasoning behind each claim and consider the principles of management and similarity that underlie them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two questions
Read the opening sentences carefully to identify the two questions posed: one soul in two bodies, and two souls in one body. Note that the author signals these investigations are obscure.
2
Analyze the argument for one soul in two bodies
Follow the reasoning: the soul's attachment to the body is by way of management, and one manager can oversee multiple domains. Then consider the pleasure-seeking motive, which would be better satisfied with more bodies, leading to the conclusion that it is at least possible.
Notice the shift from impossibility to possibility to even obligation, then qualification.
3
Analyze the argument for two souls in one body
Examine the first aspect: if souls are similar in essence and attributes, they share the same reasons for attachment, so none has priority, leading to all being attached.
The passage mentions 'from several aspects' but only gives the first; consider why this argument suffices for possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني عشر في أنه هل يعقل وجود نفس واحدة تكون متصرفة في بدنين وجود نفسين يكونان متصرفتين في بدن واحد؟ اعلم : أن هذه المباحث غامضة. ولقائل أن يقول : أما تعلق النفس الواحدة بالأبدان الكثيرة ، يجب أن لا يكون ممتنعاً . وذلك لأن تعلق النفس بالبدن ، ليس إلا على سبيل التصرف والتدبير ، وكون الشيء الواحد متصرفاً في مملكتين وفي بيتين غير ممتنع ، فوجب أن لا يمتنع ذلك . والذي يزيده تقريراً : أن السبب لعشق النفس على التعلق بالبدن : هو أن تستعمل هذه الآلات البدنية في تحصيل اللذات الجسمانية ، والراحات البدنية . ومعلوم أن استعمال بدنين أكثر وأقوى في إفادة هذا المعنى ، فوجب أن يكون تعلق النفس بالأبدان الكثيرة واجباً . فإن لم يجب ذلك ، فلا أقل من الإمكان على سبيل الندرة وأما تعلق النفوس الكثيرة بالبدن الواحد فهذا أيضا محتمل من وجوه : الأول : هو أن النفوس الكثيرة إذا كانت متماثلة في تمام الماهية ، وكانت متشابهة في الأخلاق والصفات ، فحينئذ تكون متشاركة في جميع الأمور التي لأجلها تعلقت بذلك البدن ، فلم يكن تعلق بعضها ،به ، أولى من تعلق الباقي به ، فوجب تعلقها بأسرها بذلك البدن
Chapter twelve: On whether it is conceivable that one soul exists, managing two bodies, or that two souls exist, managing one body? Know that these investigations are obscure. One may say: As for the attachment of one soul to many bodies, it should not be impossible. That is because the attachment of the soul to the body is only by way of management and administration, and the fact that one thing manages two kingdoms and two houses is not impossible, so it is necessary that it is not impossible. What strengthens this further is that the reason for the soul's love for attachment to the body is to use these bodily instruments to obtain physical pleasures and bodily comforts. It is known that using two bodies is greater and stronger in providing this meaning, so it would be necessary that the soul's attachment to many bodies is obligatory. If it is not obligatory, then at least it is possible in a rare manner. As for the attachment of many souls to one body, this is also possible from several aspects: The first is that if many souls are similar in complete essence, and are alike in character and attributes, then they share in all the matters for which they are attached to that body, so the attachment of some of them to it is not more appropriate than the attachment of the rest, so it is necessary that all of them are attached to that body.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exploration of two related questions about the soul-body relationship. The author begins by stating that the chapter discusses whether it is conceivable for one soul to manage two bodies or for two souls to manage one body. He then notes that these investigations are obscure. Next, he presents an argument for the possibility of one soul being attached to many bodies: the soul's relation to the body is one of management and administration, and it is not impossible for one manager to oversee multiple domains (e.g., two kingdoms or two houses). Therefore, the attachment of one soul to many bodies is not impossible. The argument is strengthened by the reason for the soul's attachment to the body: to use bodily instruments to obtain physical pleasures and comforts. Since using two bodies would provide these more effectively, it would be obligatory for the soul to be attached to many bodies. The author then qualifies that if it is not obligatory, it is at least possible in rare cases. Then he turns to the second question: many souls attaching to one body. He states that this is also possible from several aspects, and he gives the first aspect: if many souls are completely similar in essence, character, and attributes, then they all share the same reasons for attachment to that body, so none has priority over another, and thus all must be attached to that body.

نفس (nafs)
بدن (badan)
تعلق (ta'alluq)
تصرف (tasarruf)
تدبير (tadbir)
ماهية (mahiyya)
مماثلة (mumathala)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage affirms that one soul actually manages two bodies or two souls actually manage one body.
Correction: The passage only argues for the logical possibility, not the actual occurrence, of such arrangements. The author qualifies the arguments with 'if not obligatory, then at least possible' and presents them as dialectical.

Checkpoint

D) To achieve spiritual perfection

Key Takeaway
The passage demonstrates that rational inquiry into the soul-body relationship allows for possibilities beyond ordinary experience, grounded in principles of management and similarity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

If your soul could manage a second body, would you use it to increase your obedience to Allah or to double your indulgence in worldly desires? What does your answer reveal about your current priorities?
?
The passage suggests that souls attached to the same body would be similar in essence and attributes. Think of the people you are most attached to in this life—are you seeking souls that reflect your own, or are you drawn to those that challenge you to grow? Which kind of attachment would be more beneficial for your akhirah?
?

Are you using each limb—your eyes, tongue, hands—as a tool for divine pleasure or for temporary gratification? What step will you take today to reclaim one bodily instrument for Allah?

First Proof for the Oneness of the Soul
Al-Razi presents a cumulative proof for the oneness of the soul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's cumulative proof that the soul is a single entity underlying all perceptions and actions.

Core Idea
The soul must be one because a single subject must underlie all perception, judgment, and action.

Al-Razi presents a decisive proof for the unity of the soul by showing that a single entity must be responsible for perceiving, imagining, judging, understanding universals, and initiating voluntary action. This proof builds step by step, demonstrating that distributing these functions among multiple loci would contradict reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage has some OCR corruption; focus on the logical flow.
2
Identify the cumulative steps
The proof proceeds through several stages: perception, imagination, judgment, composition, universal application, and voluntary action. Notice that each stage ends with a call for a single subject.
Each step adds a new function but reinforces the same conclusion.
3
Trace the conclusion
After following the steps, note how al-Razi concludes that distributing powers among different loci is irrational. This is the key takeaway.
4
Reflect on the argument’s force
Consider why al-Razi calls this a 'decisive and certain proof'. What makes it compelling? How does it address potential doubts?
Think about whether any step could be challenged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل [اليامي سالم؟] في [القامة الحلقة القاهرة؟] على أن الموصوف بجميع أقسام [الإمباكات؟] والمباشر لجميع [التحريكات والتحبيبات؟] لهذا [البحن؟] : هم النفس .
نقول : الذي يدل على صحة ما ذكرناه وجوه :
الحجة الأولى : ما ذكرناه في إثبات النفس ، ولا بأس بإعادة ذلك . فنقول : إنا إذا رأينا العسل حكمنا بأنه حلو ، والقاضي على الشيئين لا بد وأن يحضره المقضي عليهما . فههنا شيء واحد يدرك جميع المحسوسات . ثم إذا تخيلناها ثم أحسسنا بها . حكمنا بأن ذلك المتخيل هو هذا المحسوس . فلا بد من شيء واحد ، هو المدرك ، وهو المتخيل . ثم إذا أحسسنا تلك الصور ، أو تخيلنا تلك الخيالات حكمنا عليها تارة بالعداوة ، وأخرى بالصداقة . فلا بد من شيء واحد هو المدرك لتلك الصور ولتلك المعاني . ثم إن القوة الفكرية تقوى على تركيب تلك الصور، وتلك المعاني ، بعضها بالبعض ، فيكون ذلك الشيء قادراً على التركيب والتحليل ، وعلى إدراك الصور والمعاني . ثم إن الإنسان يمكنه أن يحكم على كل واحد من الأشخاص بإدخاله تحت الماهية الكلية، فلا بد من شيء واحد يكون بعينه موصوفاً بالإدراكات الكلية والجزئية . ثم إن الفعل الاختياري عبارة عما إذا اعتقد في شيء كونه نافعاً ، يتولد من ذلك الاعتقاد ميل وإرادة . ويترتب على ذلك الميل : صدور الفعل عن القادر. فلا بد من شيء واحد يكون موصوفاً تلك الإدراكات الكلية والجزئية ويكون موصوفاً بالميل والإدراكات بجميع ويكون هو الموصوف بالتحريك والتدبير.
فهذا برهان قطعي يقيني لا مرية فيه في أن الموصوف بجميع الصفات ، يجب أن يكون شيئاً واحداً ، وأن توزيع هذه القوى ، وهذه الإدراكات على المحال المختلفة ، والمواضع المتباينة : قول ضد مقتضى العقل .
The chapter [？] concerning [establishing the overwhelming proof？] that the one described with all kinds of [perceptions？] and the direct agent of all [movements and animating forces？] in this [body？] is the soul.
We say: That which indicates the correctness of what we have mentioned are aspects:
The first proof: What we mentioned in proving the soul, and there is no harm in repeating that. So we say: When we see honey, we judge that it is sweet, and the judge of two things must have the two judged items present before him. So here there is a single thing that perceives all sensible objects. Then, when we imagine them, then sense them, we judge that what was imagined is this sensed thing. So there must be a single thing that is the perceiver and the imaginer. Then, when we sense those forms or imagine those images, we judge them sometimes as hostile and other times as friendly. So there must be a single thing that perceives those forms and those meanings. Then the intellectual faculty is able to compose those forms and those meanings, some with others, so that thing is capable of composition and analysis, and of perceiving forms and meanings. Then man can judge of each individual that it falls under the universal essence, so there must be a single thing that is described by universal and particular perceptions. Then voluntary action is when one believes something to be beneficial, from that belief a desire and will arise, and upon that desire follows the performance of the act by the agent. So there must be a single thing that is described by those universal and particular perceptions, described by desire and all perceptions, and is the one described as moving and managing.
This is a decisive and certain proof, no doubt in it, that the one described with all attributes must be a single thing, and that distributing these powers and perceptions among different loci and diverse places is a statement contrary to what reason demands.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents a cumulative proof (al-ḥujjah al-ūlā) for the unity of the soul. It begins by stating the thesis: the soul is the single subject of all perceptions and actions. The proof then proceeds step by step: (1) when we perceive honey's sweetness, a single thing must have both the honey and the sweetness present; (2) the same single thing perceives, imagines, and judges the identity of what was imagined and what is sensed; (3) the same single thing judges forms and images as hostile or friendly; (4) the intellectual faculty composes and analyzes, so that same thing is capable of both; (5) man applies universal essences to particulars, so a single thing has both universal and particular perceptions; (6) voluntary action involves belief, desire, and action, all in one thing. The conclusion is that the soul is one, and distributing these functions among different loci is irrational. The proof is presented as decisive and certain.

Key Terms
نفس (soul)
إدراكات كلية وجزئية (universal and particular perceptions)
فعل اختياري (voluntary action)
قوة فكرية (intellectual faculty)
برهان قطعي (decisive proof)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that different faculties (perception, imagination, judgment, etc.) are independent and could belong to different substances.
Correction: The proof shows that because these functions are interrelated—e.g., we compare imagined and sensed objects, or apply universals to particulars—they must all belong to a single subject, the soul.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what must be true about the entity that perceives, imagines, judges, and initiates voluntary action?
A) It is composed of multiple parts
B) It is a single thing
C) It is the body
D) It is the intellect alone

Key Takeaway
The soul is a single entity that underlies all perceptions and actions; distributing these functions among multiple loci contradicts reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you act out of anger or desire, do you feel a single self behind those actions, or do you feel fragmented into conflicting parts? What does this lesson reveal about the true nature of your self?
?
If your soul is one and responsible for all your perceptions and choices, where do you place your accountability when you sin? Do you blame parts of yourself, or do you accept that your single soul is fully responsible?
?
The proof shows that rational judgments and voluntary actions must come from the same entity. When you intend something, do you live as if your reason and will are in conflict, or do you align them as coming from your unified soul?

Second Proof: The Soul Knows Particulars
Al-Razi argues that if the soul manages this particular body, it must know it as a particular.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi uses the soul's management of the body to prove that it knows particulars.

Core Idea
Managing this body requires knowing it as a particular.

Al-Razi presents a logical argument that moves from the soul's management of the body to its knowledge of particulars. He first establishes that the soul is a substance separate from the body, then uses a dichotomous reasoning to show that it must manage this specific body, and therefore must know it as a particular. This proof is a key example of rational argumentation in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
Al-Razi begins with the established premise: the soul is a substance not inhering in the body. This sets the foundation that the soul is a separate entity capable of acting upon the body.
2
Follow the first dichotomy
The soul either manages this body or it does not. If it does not, there is no connection, which contradicts our experience of the soul's influence on the body. So the soul must manage it.
3
Second dichotomy: which body?
Does the soul manage the absolute (any) body or this particular body? If it managed any body, its effect would be equally present in all bodies, which is false. Therefore, it must manage this particular body.
4
Conclude knowledge of particulars
Managing this particular body requires knowledge of it as this particular. Thus the soul knows particulars.
Note that the passage ends with an objection that is not answered here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية في إثبات أن النفس مدركة للجزئيات : أن نقول : لما ثبت أن النفس جوهر ليس حالا في الجسم. فذلك الجوهر ، إما أن يكون متصرفاً في هذا البدن ومديراً له ، وإما أن لا يكون . فإن لم يوجد هذا التصرف والتدبير كان ذلك الموجود مبايناً لهذا البدن بالكلية ، ولا تعلق بينهما أصلاً . وأما إن كانت النفس مديرة للبدن ، فإما أن يكون قصد النفس تدبير مطلق البدن ، أو تدبير هذا البدن . فإن كان الأول لم يكن ظهور أثرها في هذا البدن ، أولى من ظهور ذلك الأثر في بدن آخر. فحينئذ يكون حال جميع النفوس مع جميع الأبدان على السوية . وذلك باطل قطعاً . وإما إن كان قصد النفس المعينة تدبير هذا البدن من حيث إنه هذا البدن المعين. فنقول : القصد إلى تدبير هذا البدن من حيث إنه هذا البدن المعين ، مشروط بالعلم بهذا البدن ، ولما كانت النفس تريد تدبير هذا البدن، وجب أن تكون عالمة بهذا البدن من حيث إنه هذا البدن . فتكون النفس عالمة بالجزئيات، فإن قالوا : النفس تعلم الجزئيات
The second proof for establishing that the soul perceives particulars: We say: Since it is established that the soul is a substance not inhering in the body, that substance either manages and directs this body or does not. If this management and direction does not exist, then that existent is completely separate from this body, and there is no connection between them at all. But if the soul is directing the body, then either the soul's intention is the direction of the absolute body, or the direction of this particular body. If the former, then the appearance of its effect in this body would not be more likely than the appearance of that effect in another body. Then the situation of all souls with respect to all bodies would be equal. That is absolutely false. And if the intention of the specific soul is to direct this body insofar as it is this particular body, then we say: The intention to direct this body insofar as it is this particular body is conditioned by knowledge of this body. Since the soul wants to direct this body, it must know this body insofar as it is this body. Thus the soul knows particulars. Then if they say: The soul knows particulars...
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof (al-ḥujjah al-thāniyah) that the soul perceives particulars. It begins with a premise: the soul is a substance not dwelling in the body. Then it presents a dichotomy: either the soul manages this body or it does not. If it does not, it is completely disconnected — which contradicts experience. So the soul must manage the body. Then another dichotomy: either it manages the absolute body (any body) or this particular body. If it manages the absolute body, then its effect would be equally present in all bodies, which is false. Therefore, it must manage this particular body. Managing this particular body requires knowledge of it as this particular. Hence, the soul knows particulars. The passage ends with an objection ('if they say') but the answer is not included in this window.

Key Terms
جوهر (substance)
متصرف (manager)
مدير (director)
تدبير (management)
جزئيات (particulars)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the soul only knows universals, but this proof shows it must know particulars to manage a specific body.
Correction: The soul's direct management of this particular body logically requires knowledge of it as a particular, not just universal knowledge.

Checkpoint

The soul's management of a specific body proves that it knows particulars.

?
If the soul manages this specific body, then no action is hidden from it. How does this truth confront your private moments—those deeds no human sees? Will you now live as if your soul is watching, because it is? What will you repent for right now?

Razi's Proof: The Soul Knows Particulars After Death
Razi proves the soul's knowledge of particulars is independent of bodily instruments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's rational argument that the soul's knowledge of particulars does not depend on bodily instruments and continues after death.

Core Idea
The soul's knowledge of particulars does not require bodily organs—this is proven by a logical dilemma.

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a powerful rational proof to show that the human soul, after departing the body, remains capable of knowing particular things. He uses a dichotomy and a refutation of circularity to demonstrate that knowledge of particulars cannot depend on bodily instruments. This passage establishes a key doctrine in Islamic eschatology and philosophical psychology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the rhythm, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical structure: Razi begins with a dichotomy.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main dichotomy
Razi divides the possibilities: either the soul's perceptions depend on bodily instruments or they do not. This is the core of his argument.
The first alternative leads directly to his conclusion.
3
Understand the refutation of dependency
Razi shows that if perceptions depend on instruments, it leads to circularity. He examines how the soul perceives the instrument itself—either universally or particularly—and shows both cases fail.
Focus on the circularity argument (dawr).
4
Grasp the conclusion
The conclusion is that the soul's knowledge of particulars is not dependent on bodily instruments, so after death it continues and even strengthens.
This supports the Islamic doctrine of the soul's survival after death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث عشر في بيان أن النفس بعد مفارقة البدن تبقى عالمة محركة الجزئيات. والذي يدل عليه: إن إدراكات البدن وأفعاله إما أن تكون موقوفة على الآلات الجسمانية، وإما أن لا تكون. فإن كان الحق هو الثاني، فحينئذ تكون النفس بعد مفارقة الآلات البدنية تتقوى على إدراكات الجزئيات وعلى الأفعال المخصوصة. وأما القسم الأول وهو أن يقال: إن الإدراكات الجزئية الحاصلة للنفس موقوفة على الآلات الجسمانية. فهذا باطل قطعاً وذلك لأن إدراكها لتلك الآلة إما أن يكون إدراكاً كلياً أو جزئياً. فإن كان كلياً اختصاصها بهذا البدن المعين وبهذه الآلة المعينة أولى من اختصاصها بسائر الأبدان وبسائر الآلات. وإن كان ذلك الإدراك جزئياً فحينئذ لا يكون إدراكها لتلك الآلة الشخصية من حيث إنها هي بواسطة استعمال تلك الآلة. لأن استعمالها لتلك الآلة يتوقف على إدراكها لها. فإن كان إدراكها لها متوقفاً على استعمالها لها لزم الدور وإنه محال. فثبت بما ذكرنا: إن كون النفس مدركة للجزئيات غير موقوف على الآلات الجسمانية.
The thirteenth chapter on the demonstration that the soul after separation from the body remains knowing and moving the particulars. That which indicates it: the perceptions and actions of the body are either dependent on bodily instruments, or not. If the truth is the second, then at that time the soul after separation from the bodily instruments becomes strong over the perceptions of particulars and over specific actions. As for the first division, that it is said that the partial perceptions obtained by the soul are dependent on bodily instruments; this is absolutely false, because its perception of that instrument is either a universal perception or a particular one. If it is universal, then its specification to this particular body and to this particular instrument would be more appropriate than its specification to all other bodies and all other instruments. If that perception is particular, then at that time its perception of that individual instrument is not insofar as it is it by means of using that instrument, because its use of that instrument is dependent on its perception of it. If its perception of it is dependent on its use of it, circularity would be necessary, and it is impossible. So it is established by what we have mentioned that the soul's being a perceiver of particulars is not dependent on bodily instruments.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi that the human soul, after separating from the body at death, continues to know particular things and can act upon them, and that this knowledge and action do not depend on bodily organs. The argument proceeds by presenting a dichotomy: either the soul's perceptions and actions depend on bodily instruments or they do not. If they do not depend on them, then after death the soul becomes even stronger in perceiving particulars and performing actions, which is the desired conclusion. If they do depend on bodily instruments, Razi argues that this is impossible. He refutes the dependency thesis by analyzing how the soul perceives the instrument itself. The soul's perception of the instrument must be either universal or particular. If it is universal (i.e., the soul has a general concept of the instrument), then the soul's being specifically tied to this particular body and instrument rather than any other body or instrument would require explanation—why this specific instrument? This is problematic because a universal concept does not entail a particular attachment. If the perception is particular, then the soul's perception of that specific instrument cannot be via the use of that instrument, because using the instrument presupposes already perceiving it, leading to a vicious circle (dawr): perception requires use, and use requires perception. Thus the dependency thesis is impossible. Therefore, the correct position is that the soul's knowledge of particulars is not dependent on bodily instruments, and after death it continues and even strengthens.

Key Terms
النفس
الآلات الجسمانية
الإدراكات الجزئية
الدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul's knowledge of particulars is entirely dependent on the body and ceases after death.
Correction: Razi proves that if knowledge depended on bodily instruments, a circularity would arise; therefore it is independent and continues after death.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion Razi proves in this passage?
A) The soul after death knows only universals, not particulars.
B) The soul after death continues to know particulars and does not depend on bodily instruments.
C) The soul's knowledge of particulars is impossible without bodily instruments.
D) The soul ceases to exist after death.

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that the soul's knowledge of particulars cannot depend on bodily instruments; otherwise a vicious circle arises, proving the soul's continued knowledge after death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though your soul is merely a function of your brain and body, or do you truly believe it is an independent, enduring reality? How would your daily priorities change if you acted on the certainty that your soul's knowledge and identity survive death?
?
Razi's proof shows that your soul does not need bodily instruments to know particulars. If that is true, then your deepest self-knowledge—your intentions, fears, loves—is not limited by your physical condition. Are you investing in that interior reality, or are you distracted by the instruments?
?
The argument exposes a contradiction in thinking that the body is the source of perception: it leads to circularity. Examine your own attachments—are you relying on your body, status, or possessions to define who you are? What would it mean to detach from these instruments and trust the soul's independent power?

The Soul's Awareness After Death: A Rational Proof
Proof that the soul continues to perceive particulars after death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that the soul continues to perceive particulars after death, based on the impossibility of dependence on bodily instruments.

Core Idea
The soul's perception of particulars does not depend on the body, so it survives death.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a powerful logical argument to prove that the human soul remains aware of individual things after leaving the body. He systematically eliminates the possibility that the soul's perceptions depend on physical instruments. This lesson will walk through his disjunctive proof and show why it is considered a foundational principle in the science of the afterlife (ma‘ād).

Guided Path
1
Understand the thesis and the disjunction
The passage states: either the soul's perceptions depend on bodily instruments or not. If not, the conclusion follows directly. If they do, then we must examine that claim.
2
Explore the two possibilities for perceiving the instrument
If the soul's perception of the instrument is universal, then attachment to a specific body is arbitrary. If particular, then circularity arises.
3
Recognize the circularity (دور) argument
Using the instrument requires perceiving it, but perceiving it would require using it, leading to impossibility.
Circularity (دور) is a logical fallacy where A depends on B and B depends on A.
4
Conclude that the soul's perception is independent
Thus the dependence premise is false, and the soul survives.
5
Connect to the hadith and the science of the afterlife
The author confirms with prophetic tradition and notes the importance for ma‘ād.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل [؟] سكر . بيان أن النفس بعد مفارقة البدن تبقى عالمة محركة الجزئيات . والذي يدل عليه : إن إدراكات البدن وأفعاله . إما أن تكون موقوفة على الآلات الجسمانية ، وإما أن لا تكون . فإن كان الحق هو الثاني ، فحينئذ تكون النفس بعد مفارقة الآلات البدنية تتقوى على إدراكات الجزئينات . وعلى الأفعال المخصوصة . وأما القسم الأول وهو أن يقال : إن الإدراكات الجزئية الحاصلة للنفس ، موقوفة على الآلات الجسمانية . فهذا باطل قطعاً وذلك لأن إدراكها لتلك الآلة ، إما أن يكون إدراكاً كلياً أو جزئياً. فإن كان كلياً اختصاصها بهذا البدن المعين ، وبهذه الآلة المعينة ، أولى من اختصاصها بسائر الأبدان ، وسائر الآلات . وإن كان ذلك الأمر إدراكاً جزئياً ، فحينئذ لا يكون إدراكها لتلك الآلة الشخصية ، من حيث إنها هي بواسطة استعمال تلك الآلة . لأن استعمالها لتلك الآلة ، يتوقف على إدراكها لها . فإن كان إدراكها لها متوقفاً على استعمالها لها ، لزم الدور. وإنه محال . فثبت بما ذكرنا : إن كون النفس مدركة للجزئيات ، غير موقوف على الآلات الجسمانية . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، وجب القطع بأن النفس بعد مفارقة البدن ، تبقى مدركة للجزئيات . وهذا أصل شريف منتفع به في علم المعاد . وبهذا يظهر صدق قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( حتى إذا حمل الميت على نعشه ، رفرفت روحه فوق النعش . وتقول : يا أهلي ويا ولدي . لا تلعبن بكم الدنيا ، كما لعبت بي . جمعت المال من حله ومن غير حله . فالمهنا لغيري ، والتبعة علي . فاحذروا مثل ما حل بي ) . وهذا الفصل ، وإن كان صغير الحجم ، إلا أنه عظيم النفع . والله أعلم .
Chapter [?]. Statement that the soul after separation from the body remains knowing and moving particulars. What indicates it: The perceptions and actions of the body are either dependent on physical instruments or not dependent. If the correct is the second, then at that time the soul after separation from bodily instruments becomes stronger in perceiving particulars and performing specific actions. As for the first division—that is, to say that the particular perceptions occurring to the soul are dependent on physical instruments—this is absolutely false. That is because its perception of that instrument is either a universal perception or a particular perception. If it is universal, then its being specifically attached to this particular body and to this particular instrument is more likely than its attachment to other bodies and other instruments. And if that matter is a particular perception, then at that time its perception of that particular instrument is not by virtue of it being that instrument through using that instrument, because its use of that instrument depends on its perception of it. For if its perception of it were dependent on its use of it, a circularity would arise, and it is impossible. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned that the soul's being a perceiver of particulars is not dependent on physical instruments. And if the matter is so, it is necessary to conclude that the soul after separation from the body remains perceiving particulars. This is a noble principle from which benefit is derived in the science of the afterlife. And by this is shown the truth of his statement, peace be upon him: 'When the deceased is carried on his bier, his spirit flutters above the bier and says: O my family, O my children! Let not the world distract you as it distracted me. I gathered wealth from lawful and unlawful means. Now the enjoyment is for others, and the burden is upon me. So beware of what has befallen me.' And this chapter, though small in size, is great in benefit. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a proof (argument) demonstrating that the soul remains aware of particulars after death. The author begins by stating the topic: the soul after leaving the body remains knowing and moving particulars. He then presents a disjunctive argument: either the soul's perceptions and actions depend on bodily instruments or they do not. If they do not depend, then after separation the soul becomes even stronger in perceiving particulars. If they do depend, then that position is false because of an impossibility. He explains: if perceptions depend on bodily instruments, then the soul's perception of that instrument must be either universal or particular. If it is universal, then the soul's attachment to this specific body is arbitrary and no more justified than attachment to any other body. If it is particular, then perception of the instrument would require prior use of that instrument, but use depends on perception, leading to circularity (دور), which is impossible. Therefore, the premise of dependence is false. The author concludes that the soul's perception of particulars is not dependent on bodily instruments, so after death the soul remains perceiving particulars. He then declares this a beneficial principle for the science of the afterlife (علم المعاد), and supports it with a prophetic hadith describing the soul's awareness after death. He ends by noting the chapter's small size but great benefit.

الجزئيات
الآلات الجسمانية
الدور
علم المعاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument denies that the soul uses the body in this life at all.
Correction: The argument does not deny that the soul uses the body; it shows that its essential capacity to perceive particulars does not depend on bodily instruments, so it survives death.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The soul's perception of particulars is independent of the body, so it continues after death, which is a foundational principle for the science of the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul right now could see your life as it will after death—without the distraction of the body—what would it be ashamed of? What would it plead with you to change before it's too late?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) described the soul of the deceased warning its family: 'Let not the world distract you as it distracted me.' Are you in any way allowing the world to distract you from preparing for that moment when your soul will cry out the same?
?
You have just learned that your soul perceives and knows more after death than now. If this awareness filled your heart as a certainty, what would you stop doing today? What would you start doing?

The Sixth Argument: Spiritual Unveilings and Supplication
Presents the sixth argument: spiritual unveilings either weaken desire for worldly things or are absent, making supplication useless.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth argument against the efficacy of supplication, which divides the state of the supplicant based on spiritual unveilings and concludes that supplication is either meaningless or futile.

Core Idea
Supplication is useless: either it's empty talk or you're too absorbed in divine lights to want anything.

In this passage, the author presents a formidable challenge to the practice of supplication. The argument claims that true benefit from supplication requires spiritual unveilings (mukashafat), but such unveilings either make worldly goals appear insignificant or are entirely absent. This creates a dilemma that seems to undermine the very purpose of du'a.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic original and the literal translation once without analysis. Let the argument's structure become clear.
Notice the binary division at the start.
2
Identify the two main branches
The passage first divides supplicants into those who have spiritual unveilings and those who do not. Find this division.
3
Examine the case of no unveiling
If no unveiling, the supplication is merely 'movement of the tongue' with no benefit except increasing 'prattle'.
This is a strong criticism.
4
Examine the case of unveiling
If unveiling occurs, it branches further: if the unveiling is strong, the soul is absorbed in divine lights and loses interest in worldly things; if weak, the acquired strength is insufficient.
In both sub-cases, supplication fails to achieve worldly aims.
5
Reflect on the overall conclusion
The argument concludes that supplication is either futile (no unveiling) or ineffective (unveiling weakens desire or is too weak). Consider why this is a serious objection.
This will be refuted later, but understand its force.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة: إن المشتغل بالدعاء إما أن يكون قد حصل في قلبه نوع من المكاشفات الروحانية أو لم يحصل ذلك. فإن لم يحصل ذلك كان ذلك الدعاء مجرد تحريك اللسان ولا فائدة فيه إلا تكثير الهذيان. وإن حصل فيه ذلك الكشف فإن كان الكشف قوياً تاماً صارت النفس مستغرقة في تلك الأضواء والأنوار تبقى النفس ذلك المقدار من ذلك الكشف طالبة لهذه الأغراض الجسمانية راغبة في تحصيلها كانت تلك القوة الحاصلة من تلك المكاشفة ضعيفة جداً. وحينئذ لا تفيد شيئاً.
The sixth argument: The one engaged in supplication, either some type of spiritual unveilings has occurred in his heart or it has not occurred. If it has not occurred, then that supplication is merely the movement of the tongue and there is no benefit in it except increasing prattle. And if that unveiling has occurred in him, then if the unveiling is strong and complete, the soul becomes absorbed in those lights and illuminations, the soul [remains?] that amount of that unveiling seeking these bodily purposes desiring to obtain them, but that strength acquired from that unveiling is very weak. And then it does not benefit anything.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth objection, focusing on the internal state of the supplicant. It divides the case into two possibilities: either the person has experienced spiritual unveilings (mukashafat) or not. If not, their supplication is just empty words. If they have such unveilings, two sub-cases: if the unveiling is strong, the soul is so absorbed in divine lights that it loses interest in worldly goals, so supplication for worldly things is inconsistent. If the unveiling is weak, the resulting spiritual strength is insufficient to effect anything. Thus, supplication is either meaningless or ineffective.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is taken as proof that supplication is never beneficial.
Correction: This is an objection that the author will later refute; the passage does not represent the final position but a challenge to be answered.

Checkpoint

A) Their supplication is still effective due to God's mercy.
B) Their supplication is mere tongue movement with no benefit except increasing prattle.
C) They should seek unveiling before supplicating.
D) Their supplication is accepted if they have faith.

Key Takeaway
The sixth argument challenges supplication by claiming it only benefits those with spiritual unveilings, but even then it is ineffective for worldly goals.
