Angels as Immaterial Beings: Two Views
Classification of two views on immaterial angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major views on angels as immaterial beings: the Christian identification with rational souls and the philosophical classification into celestial souls and separate intellects.

Core Idea
Angels as immaterial beings: either purified human souls or transcendent intellects.

This lesson presents the second major classification of angels: those considered immaterial and self-subsistent. The author outlines two distinct views: one from Christian theology that equates angels with disembodied rational souls, and another from the philosophers who define angels as abstract substances far superior to human souls. Additionally, the philosophical view further divides these beings into those managing the celestial spheres and those entirely beyond the physical world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how the author structures the two opinions clearly.
Pay attention to the technical terms like 'جواهر مجردة' (immaterial substances).
2
Identify the two views
The passage presents two main statements (قولان). Identify what they are and who holds each view.
3
Examine the Christian view
Understand how Christians identify angels with rational souls (النفوس الناطقة) separated from bodies, and how they distinguish angels from devils by purity.
This view makes angels essentially human souls in a purified state.
4
Examine the philosophical view
See how philosophers define angels as immaterial substances (جواهر مجردة) superior to human souls. Then note the two subtypes: celestial souls (النفوس الفلكية) and separate intellects (العقول المجردة).
Celestial souls manage bodies like spheres; separate intellects have no connection to bodies.
5
Reflect on the differences
Compare the two views. Consider how each understands the relationship between angels, souls, and the physical world.
The author notes that the philosophers' proofs are covered elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقسم الثاني : وهو ان الملائكة ذوات قائمة بأنفسها . وليست متحيزة ولا حالة في المتحيزات ، ففيه قولان : الأول : قول طوائف من النصارى : وهو أن الملائكة في الحقيقة : هي الأنفس الناطقة ، المفارقة لأبدانها مع المفارقة لأبدانها مع الصفاء والخيرية . وذلك لأن هذه النفوس المفارقة ، إن كانت صافية خيرة ، فهي الملائكة . وإن كانت خبيثة كدرة ، فهي الشياطين . والثاني : وهو قول جمهور الفلاسفة : إن الملائكة عبارة عن جواهر مجردة عن الجسمية وعلائقها . وإنها بالماهية مخالفة للنوفس البشرية [ ولا نسبة لعلومها إلى علوم النفوس البشرية الناطقة ولا لقدرها إلى قدر النفوس الناطقة البشرية . وأنها أكمل منها قوة وأكثر علماً . وأنها بالنسبة إلى النفوس البشرية جارية مجرى الشمس بالنسبة ] إلى الضوء القليل ، والبحر الأعظم بالنسبة إلى القطرة ثم إن هذه الجواهر على قسمين : منها ما هي مستقلة بتدبير أجسام الأفلاك والكواكب . كنفوسنا الناطقة بالنسبة إلى أبداننا [ ] وهي المسماة بالنفوس الفلكية . ومنها ما هو أعلى شأناً من أن يكون لها تعلق بعالم الأجسام . وهي العقول المجردة. وقد ذكر دلائل الفلاسفة في إثبات هذه الموجودات على سبيل الاستقصاء .
And the second division: that the angels are self-subsistent entities. They are not material nor inhere in material things. There are two statements concerning this: The first is the statement of groups of Christians: that the angels in reality are the rational souls, separate from their bodies, along with purity and goodness. This is because these separate souls, if they are pure and good, they are angels; and if they are evil and turbid, they are devils. The second is the statement of the majority of philosophers: that angels are substances abstracted from corporeality and its attachments. They are essentially different from human souls. [There is no proportion of their knowledge to the knowledge of rational human souls, nor of their power to the power of rational human souls. They are more perfect in power and greater in knowledge. They are in relation to human souls like the sun in relation to] little light, and like the great ocean in relation to the drop. Then these substances are of two kinds: some are independent in managing the bodies of the spheres and planets, like our rational souls in relation to our bodies [which are called celestial souls]. And some are higher in rank to have any connection to the world of bodies, and they are the separate intellects. And the philosophers' proofs for establishing these existents have been mentioned exhaustively.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage presents the second main division of views on angels: those who consider angels as immaterial, self-subsistent entities. Two sub-views are given. First, the Christian view identifies angels with rational souls separated from bodies, distinguishing them from devils by purity. Second, the philosophical view defines angels as immaterial substances (جواهر مجردة) that are superior to human souls. The philosophers further divide these substances into two categories: (1) celestial souls (النفوس الفلكية) that manage celestial bodies, analogous to human souls managing bodies; (2) separate intellects (العقول المجردة) that are too exalted to be connected to the corporeal world. The author notes that the philosophers' proofs have been fully covered.

العقول المجردة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Confusing the Christian and philosophical views, thinking both identify angels with human souls.
Correction: The Christian view equates angels with rational souls (human souls after death), while the philosophical view sees angels as distinct, superior immaterial substances (جواهر مجردة) that are not human souls.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, what are the two types of immaterial substances that constitute angels?
A) Celestial souls and separate intellects

C) Material and immaterial

Key Takeaway
The two main immaterial views on angels are the Christian view (angels as pure rational souls) and the philosophical view (angels as transcendent intellects and celestial souls).

?

?

?
The Christian view suggests that a soul can become an angel if purified. Does your own understanding of the soul's potential align more with that or with the philosophical view that angels are a wholly different kind of being? What does your answer reveal about how you see the relationship between humans and the divine realm?

The Vast Multitude and Highest Ranks of Angels
The author cites hadith and Quranic verses describing the vast numbers and different ranks of angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence for the vast number of angels and the highest rank among them, the bearers of the Throne.

Core Idea
The angels are so numerous that all creation is but a drop compared to them.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah gathers hadith and Quranic verses to impress upon the reader the sheer scale of the angelic creation. Through a chain of ratios and a description of the heavens filled with worshiping angels, the author shows that angelic numbers far exceed human imagination. The lesson also highlights the highest rank: the bearers of the Throne.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hadith on the Heavens
Start by reading the Prophet's statement that the heavens groaned because every place is occupied by an angel in prostration or bowing. This establishes the foundation that angels fill every part of the heavens.
2
Follow the Ratio Chain
Trace the series of comparisons: humans are a tenth of jinn, jinn and humans are a tenth of land animals, and so on up to the angels of the seventh heaven. Notice how each category is dwarfed by the next.
The ratios are not literal but convey exponential vastness.
3
Ascend to the Throne Angels
Observe that even the angels of the seven heavens are negligible compared to the angels of the Kursi and then the angels of the canopies of the Arsh. This shows the immense hierarchy.
4
Contemplate the Beyond
The passage concludes that all these angels are like a drop in the ocean compared to angels of other worlds. Then it quotes the Quran about the eight bearers of the Throne, the highest rank.
Reflect on how this inspires awe of Allah's majesty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن الأخبار الكثيرة واردة في شرح كثرتها . قال عليه السلام : ه أطت السموات . وحق لها أن تنط . ما فيها موضع قدم ، إلا وفيه ملك ساجد أو راكع ) . وروى أنه بني آدم : عشر الجن . ثم إن الجن وبني آدم : عشر حيوانات البر والطير . وهؤلاء كلهم عشر حيوانات البحر . وكلهم عشر ملائكة الأرض . وكلهم عشر ملائكة السماء الدنيا . وكلهم عشر ملائكة السماء الثانية ) . وعلى هذا الترتيب إلى ملائكة السماء السابعة ، ثم الكل في مقابلة ملائكة الكرسي : شيء قليل جدا . ثم كلهم عشر ملائكة والسرادق الواحد ، من سرادقات العرش ، ثم إنه ما من مقدار من أجزاء السموات السبع والكرسي والعرش . إلا وفيه ملك ساجد ، أو راكع ، أو قائم ولهم زجل بالتسبيح والتقديس . ثم كل هؤلاء في مقابلة الملائكة - الذين سكان سائر العوالم الموجودة خارج هذا العالم - كالقطرة في البحر ، والذرة في الأرض . ولا يعلم عددهم إلا الله عز وجل واعلم : أن الله تعالى ذكر في القرآن : أصنافهم وأوصافهم . هم . أما الأصناف : فأعلاهم درجة : حملة العرش. وهو قوله : ( ويحمل عرش ربك فوقهم يومئذ ثمانية )
And know that many reports have come explaining their multitude. He (peace be upon him) said: 'The heavens groaned, and they had a right to groan. There is no place for a foot therein except that there is an angel prostrating or bowing.' And it is narrated that the children of Adam are one-tenth of the jinn. Then the jinn and the children of Adam are one-tenth of the land animals and birds. And all of these are one-tenth of the sea animals. And all of them are one-tenth of the angels of the earth. And all of them are one-tenth of the angels of the lowest heaven. And all of them are one-tenth of the angels of the second heaven, and so on up to the angels of the seventh heaven. Then all of them in comparison to the angels of the Throne (al-Kursi) are a very small thing. Then all of them are one-tenth of the angels of a single canopy among the canopies of the Throne (al-ʿArsh). Then there is no measure of the parts of the seven heavens, the Throne (al-Kursi), and the Throne (al-ʿArsh) except that there is an angel prostrating, or bowing, or standing, and they have a buzzing sound of glorification and sanctification. Then all of these in comparison to the angels who are inhabitants of the other worlds existing outside this world are like a drop in the ocean and an atom on the earth. And none knows their number except Allah Almighty. And know that Allah Almighty mentioned in the Quran their types and descriptions. They are: As for the types: the highest in rank are the bearers of the Throne (al-ʿArsh), and that is His saying: 'And the angels will be on its sides, and eight will bear the Throne of your Lord above them that Day.'
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage compiles scriptural evidence for the immense number of angels. It begins with a hadith emphasizing that every part of the heavens is filled with angels in worship. Then it presents a chain of ratios showing the relative numbers: humans are a tenth of jinn, jinn and humans are a tenth of land animals, etc., culminating in angels of the higher realms. The ratios are meant to stress that the angels of each successive realm are exponentially more numerous. Then it mentions that even all these angels are negligible compared to the angels of the throne and beyond. Finally, it cites the Quranic verse (69:17) to show that the highest rank is the bearers of the Throne. The author thus reinforces the transcendence and majesty of Allah by demonstrating the vastness of the angelic creation.

Key Terms
أطت السموات
حملة العرش
الكرسي
العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The ratios in the hadith are exact mathematical proportions.
Correction: The ratios are intended to convey vastness and hierarchy, not precise numbers.

Checkpoint

C) The first heaven angels are ten times more

Key Takeaway
The angels are immeasurably numerous, and the highest rank among them are the bearers of the Throne, as mentioned in the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The heavens groan with the weight of angels in constant worship. When was the last time your own prostration felt like a burden you carried willingly? What would it take for you to join that ceaseless glorification of Allah in your daily life? Commit to one extra act of worship today that requires physical effort, like a prolonged sujood or a night prayer.
?
If you are but a drop compared to the vast oceans of angels, how does that recalibrate your sense of self-importance? Write down one area of your life where you have been acting as if your own judgment outweighs Allah's command. Then seek forgiveness and surrender that matter to Him before you sleep tonight.
?
The angels of the highest realms are unknown to you, yet they are known to Allah. Are you content with being known by Allah even if the world overlooks you? Identify one hidden good deed you can do today solely for Allah's sight, and do it with the awareness that it is recorded among the angels' witness.

The Ratios of Creation: Angels Among the Multitudes
The author cites traditions with descending ratios from humans to angels of the seventh heaven.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophetic traditions use numerical ratios to illustrate the overwhelming number of angels relative to other creations.

Core Idea
Angels outnumber all creation by staggering ratios.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents a series of prophetic reports that use a descending scale of one-tenth to show how each category of beings is vastly outnumbered by the next. Starting from humans and jinn, the ratios climb through animals, sea creatures, and eventually to the angels of the heavens. This lesson explores the first part of that chain.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opening hadith
Read the hadith about the heavens groaning with angels. This sets the tone for the density of angelic presence.
2
Trace the chain of ratios
Starting from humans as one-tenth of jinn, follow the chain up to the angels of the seventh heaven. Each step multiplies by ten.
These ratios are not literal but relative measures.
3
Ask: What do these ratios teach?
Consider why the author presents these numbers. They emphasize that Allah's creation is vast beyond human comprehension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الأخبار الكثيرة واردة في شرح كثرتها قال عليه السلام أطت السموات وحق لها أن تئن ما فيها موضع قدم إلا وفيه ملك ساجد أو راكع وروي أن بني آدم عشر الجن ثم إن الجن وبني آدم عشر حيوانات البر والطير وهؤلاء كلهم عشر حيوانات البحر وكلهم عشر ملائكة الأرض وكلهم عشر ملائكة السماء الدنيا وكلهم عشر ملائكة السماء الثانية وعلى هذا الترتيب إلى ملائكة السماء السابعة ثم الكل في مقابلة ملائكة الكرسي شيء قليل جدا ثم كلهم عشر ملائكة والسرادق الواحد من سرادقات العرش ثم إنه ما من مقدار من أجزاء السموات السبع والكرسي والعرش إلا وفيه ملك ساجد أو راكع أو قائم ولهم زجل بالتسبيح والتقديس ثم كل هؤلاء في مقابلة الملائكة الذين سكان سائر العوالم الموجودة خارج هذا العالم كالقطرة في البحر والذرة في الأرض ولا يعلم عددهم إلا الله عز وجل.
And know: abundant reports have come in explaining their multitude. He (peace be upon him) said: 'The heavens groaned, and they had the right to groan; there is not a foot's space in them except that there is an angel prostrating or bowing.' And it is narrated that the children of Adam are one-tenth of the jinn; then the jinn and the children of Adam are one-tenth of the land animals and birds; and all of these are one-tenth of the sea animals; and all of them are one-tenth of the angels of the earth; and all of them are one-tenth of the angels of the lowest heaven; and all of them are one-tenth of the angels of the second heaven; and so on up to the angels of the seventh heaven; then all of them compared to the angels of the Footstool are very little; then all of them are one-tenth of the angels of a single canopy from the canopies of the Throne; then there is no measure of the parts of the seven heavens, the Footstool, and the Throne except that there is in it an angel prostrating, bowing, or standing, and they have a chant of glorification and sanctification. Then all of these compared to the angels who are the inhabitants of the other worlds existing outside this world are like a drop in the ocean and an atom on earth. And none knows their number except Allah, the Mighty and Majestic.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of prophetic traditions illustrating the enormous number of angels. It begins with a hadith about heaven groaning due to the density of angels. Then a series of comparisons shows the proportion of humans to jinn to various creatures to angels, each category being one-tenth of the next, culminating in the angels of the Throne and beyond. The purpose is to emphasize the vastness of Allah's creation and the limited human comprehension.

Correction: The ratios are not literal but relative measures to convey the vastness of angelic numbers beyond human grasp.

?

?
The author’s purpose in presenting these ratios is not to satisfy your curiosity but to instill awe. Has your heart trembled at the overwhelming majesty of Allah’s creation? If not, what will you do to make this lesson a reality in your heart, not just in your mind?

The Angels of the Throne and Beyond
The author scales up the angelic hierarchy to the Footstool, Throne, and beyond.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the angels of the Footstool and Throne outnumber all prior creation, and how the total number of angels is beyond comprehension.

Core Idea
The angels of the Throne dwarf all other angels, and ultimately only Allah knows their count.

After establishing the ratios up to the seventh heaven, the author escalates the scale: the angels of the Footstool far outweigh all previous angels, and the angels of the Throne's canopies are even more. The passage culminates by stating that every part of the Throne contains angels, and that all these are but a drop compared to angels in other worlds. This lesson completes the picture of angelic multitudes.

Guided Path
1
Compare seventh heaven angels to Footstool angels
The passage states that all prior angels are very little compared to the angels of the Footstool.
2
Examine the canopies of the Throne
The Footstool angels themselves are only one-tenth of the angels of a single canopy of the Throne.
3
Note the ubiquity of angels in heavenly parts
Every part of the heavens, Footstool, and Throne contains angels in prostration, bowing, or standing, glorifying Allah.
4
Understand the final comparison to other worlds
All these angels are like a drop in the ocean compared to the angels of other worlds, and only Allah knows their number.

Correction: The passage states there are angels in other worlds beyond our universe, and their numbers are unimaginable.

?

?
The passage says that all the angels we know of are like a drop in the ocean compared to angels in other worlds, and that only Allah knows their number. How does this vastness affect your understanding of Allah's majesty? Do you truly feel small before Him, or do you allow worldly concerns to inflate your self-importance? Commit to one daily action that reminds you of your place before the Creator.
?
If angels fill every part of creation in humble worship, and you are the only creation that can choose to disobey, what does that say about your responsibility? Are you using your free will to honour Allah as the angels do, or are you neglecting your purpose? Write down one area of your life where you will strive to align your actions with the worship that surrounds you.

The Three Highest Ranks of Angels
Classification of highest angels into three ranks with Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic classification of the highest angels into three distinct ranks.

Core Idea
The highest angels are ranked by proximity to Allah's Throne.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents a clear, Quran-based classification of the highest angels. The author identifies three ranks, each supported by a specific verse. Understanding this hierarchy helps us appreciate the grandeur of angelic worship and service.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the use of 'أما' to introduce the enumeration.
2
Identify the three ranks
The passage lists three ranks. Find each one and note the Quranic verse cited as evidence.
The ranks are: (1) bearers of the Throne, (2) those surrounding the Throne, (3) the great angels.
3
Understand the proof structure
For each rank, the author provides a proof text from the Quran. Notice how he summarises the verse without quoting it in full.
This is a common pattern in kalam: claim followed by scriptural evidence.
4
Reflect on the hierarchy
Think about why the bearers of the Throne are the highest, then those surrounding it, then the great angels. What does this imply about their roles?
The Throne is the greatest creation, so those closest to it are highest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الله تعالى ذكر في القرآن أصنافهم وأوصافهم أما الأصناف فأعلاهم درجة حملة العرش وهو قوله ويحمل عرش ربك فوقهم يومئذ ثمانية والمرتبة الثانية الحافون حول العرش وهو قوله تعالى وترى الملائكة حافين من حول العرش والمرتبة الثالثة أكابر الملائكة ومنهم جبريل عليه السلام وصفاته في القرآن كثيرة.
And know that Allah the Exalted has mentioned in the Quran their types and their attributes. As for the types: the highest in degree are the bearers of the Throne, and that is His saying: 'And eight will bear the Throne of your Lord above them on that Day.' The second rank: those surrounding the Throne, and that is His saying: 'And you see the angels surrounding the Throne.' The third rank: the great angels, and among them is Jibril, peace be upon him, and his attributes in the Quran are many.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage classifies the highest angels into three ranks using Quranic evidence. It is a structured enumeration: (1) Bearers of the Throne, citing Surah Al-Haqqah (69:17). (2) Those surrounding the Throne, citing Surah Az-Zumar (39:75). (3) The great angels, including Jibril, setting up the subsequent discussion of his attributes.

أكابر الملائكة

Correction: The passage explicitly states these are the highest degrees, not an exhaustive list of all ranks.

A) The bearers of the Throne
B) Those surrounding the Throne
C) The great angels
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The highest angels are ranked by proximity to the Throne: bearers, those surrounding it, and other great angels like Jibril.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Seeing that closeness to the Throne determines rank among angels, ask yourself: what is the measure of your nearness to Allah? Are you striving for proximity through obedience, or are you satisfied with distance? What step will you take tonight to draw closer?

The Second and Third Ranks of Angels
Describes the second and third ranks of angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two higher ranks of angels mentioned in the Quran and their significance.

Core Idea
The greatest angels surround the Throne or belong to the elite ranks.

In this passage, the author outlines the hierarchy of angels, focusing on the second rank (those surrounding the Throne) and the third rank (the great angels). This sets the stage for understanding the special status of Jibril among them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about ranks
Read the Arabic passage once without overanalyzing. Then read the translation. Focus on the two ranks mentioned.
Notice that the third rank is introduced as 'great angels' with Jibril as an example.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
For the second rank, find the Quranic verse cited. For the third rank, note that no specific verse is given here, but Jibril is singled out.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why knowing the ranks of angels matters for understanding Islamic theology. The commentary will help.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرتبة الثانية : الحافون حول العرش . وهو قوله تعالى : ( وترى الملائكة حافين من حول العرش )
والمرتبة الثالثة : أكابر الملائكة . ومنهم جبريل - عليه السلام - وصفاته في القرآن كثيرة .
إحداها : إنه صاحب الوحي إلى الأنبياء قال الله تعالى : نزل به الروح الأمين على قلبك
وثانيها : إنه تعالى قدمه في الذكر على ميكائيل ، فقال : ( من كان عدوا الله وملائكته ورسله وجبريل وميكائيل ) والسبب فيه : أن جبريل صاحب الوحي والعلم . وميكائيل صاحب الأغذية ، والأرزاق الجسمانية والخيرات النفسانية أفضل من الخيرات الجسمانية فلا جرم كان جبريل أفضل من ميكائيل .
ثالثها : إنه تعالى جعل جبريل ثاني نفسه . فقال : ( فإن الله هو مولاه وجبريل وصالح المؤمنين )
ورابعها : إنه سماه و روح القدس ، فقال : ( إذا أيدتك بروح القدس )
وخامسها : إنه ينصر أولياء الله ، ويقهر أعداء الله . مثل : قصة بدر
وسادسها : إنه مدحه بصفات ست . فقال : ( إنه لقول رسول كريم ، ذي قوة ، عند ذي العرش ، مكين، مطاع، ثم أمين ) ورسالته : أنه رسول الله إلى جميع الأنبياء والرسل والأنبياء كلهم من البشر . وكرمه على عباد الله تعالى : أن جعله واسطة بينه وبين أشرف عباده في الأرض . وهم الأنبياء والحكماء. وقوته : أنه ما أخل بشيء من طاعات ربه أصلا . ومكانته عند الله : أنه مستغرق في تلك العبودية ، غير ملتفت إلى شيء آخر من الأغراض . وكونه مطاعاً : أنه إمام الملائكة وأستاذهم . وكونه أميناً : فهو قوله نزل به الروح الأمين على قلبك
Second rank: those surrounding the throne. And it is His saying Exalted: (And you see the angels surrounding the throne from around it). And the third rank: the great angels. Among them is Jibril – peace be upon him – and his attributes in the Quran are many. First: He is the bearer of revelation to the prophets. Allah Exalted said: The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it upon your heart. Second: He Exalted mentioned him before Mika'il, saying: (Whoever is an enemy to Allah, His angels, His messengers, and Jibril and Mika'il). The reason is that Jibril is the bearer of revelation and knowledge, and Mika'il is the bearer of sustenance, bodily provisions, and spiritual good things are better than bodily good things, so necessarily Jibril is better than Mika'il. Third: He Exalted made Jibril second to Himself, saying: (For Allah is his Protector, and Jibril, and the righteous of the believers). Fourth: He named him the Holy Spirit, saying: (When I supported you with the Holy Spirit). Fifth: He supports the allies of Allah and subdues the enemies of Allah, such as the story of Badr. Sixth: He praised him with six attributes, saying: (Indeed it is the word of a noble messenger, possessed of strength, with the Lord of the Throne, secure, obeyed, then trustworthy). His being a messenger: he is the messenger of Allah to all prophets and messengers, and all prophets are from humans. His honour with the servants of Allah Exalted: He made him an intermediary between Himself and the most honourable of His servants on earth, and they are the prophets and the wise. His strength: he never neglected any of his Lord's acts of obedience at all. His status with Allah: he is absorbed in that worship, not turning to any other purposes. His being obeyed: he is the leader of the angels and their teacher. His being trustworthy: it is His saying: The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it upon your heart.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage classifies angels into ranks and then enumerates the attributes of Jibril. First, it mentions the second rank: angels who surround the throne, citing Quran 39:75. Then it describes the third rank: the great angels, with Jibril as a primary example. The bulk of the passage lists six attributes of Jibril with Quranic evidence. The first attribute: he is the bearer of revelation (26:193-194). The second: Allah mentioned Jibril before Mika'il in Quran 2:98, and explains that Jibril is superior because he conveys revelation and knowledge, while Mika'il provides sustenance—spiritual goods are better than bodily ones. The third: Allah made Jibril second to Himself in Quran 66:4, indicating his high rank. The fourth: Jibril is called the Holy Spirit (5:110). The fifth: Jibril helps Allah's allies and defeats His enemies, as at Badr. The sixth: Allah praised Jibril with six attributes in Quran 81:19-21 (noble messenger, strong, secure with the Lord of the Throne, obeyed, trustworthy). The text then explains each of these six: his mission as messenger to all prophets, his honour as intermediary, his strength in obedience, his absorption in worship, his leadership of angels, and his trustworthiness. The passage follows the order of the Quranic verse and elaborates each point.

Key Terms
المرتبة الثانية
المرتبة الثالثة
أكابر الملائكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All angels are of the same rank.
Correction: The Quran distinguishes ranks, such as those surrounding the Throne (second rank) and the great angels (third rank).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which rank includes angels that surround the Throne?
A) First rank
B) Second rank
C) Third rank
D) Fourth rank

Key Takeaway
Angels are ranked; the second rank surrounds the Throne, and the third rank includes the great angels like Jibril.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Six Quranic Attributes of Jibril

Israfeel and Azrael: Roles and a Philosophical Allegory
Introduces Azrael and Israfeel as great angels, cites Quranic evidence, then relates a philosophical allegory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional Islamic roles of the angels Azrael and Israfeel, and be introduced to a philosophical allegory that reinterprets them as celestial souls.

Core Idea
Angels have defined roles in scripture; philosophers sometimes allegorize them as cosmic principles.

This passage presents two of the great angels: Azrael, the Angel of Death, and Israfeel, the master of the trumpet. After citing Quranic evidence for their functions, the author reports a philosophical allegory that reinterprets them as universal souls of planetary spheres. The aim is not to endorse this allegory but to show its existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the roles of Azrael and Israfeel
Read the passage carefully and note what specific functions are attributed to each angel based on the reports and Quranic verses cited.
Azrael is the Angel of Death; Israfeel is the master of the trumpet.
2
Note the Quranic evidence
Find the three Quranic verses quoted and understand how each supports the role of the respective angel.
Verses: 32:11 (Azrael), 6:61 and 8:50 (assistants), 39:68 (Israfeel).
3
Understand the philosophical allegory
Read the philosophical interpretation that equates Azrael and Israfeel with the universal souls of Saturn and the sun, and their 'followers' with branching souls. Consider how this differs from the literal scriptural view.
This allegory is reported without endorsement; it is not orthodox.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جملة أكابر الملائكة : إسرافيل وعزرائيل عليهما السلام . والأخبار الكثيرة دلت عليها . وثبت في الأخبار : أن عزرائيل هو ملك الموت . قال تعالى : ( قل يتوفـاكم ملك الموت ) ويجب أن يكون له شعب ونتائج وأعوان . كما قال تعالى : ( حتى إذا جاء أحدكم الموت . توفته رسلنا وهم لا يفرطون ) وقال تعالى : ( ولو ترى إذ يتوفى الذين كفروا . الملائكة يضربون وجوههم وأدبارهم ) وأما إسرافيل عليه السلام فقد دلت الأخبار على أنه صاحب الصور ، كما قال : ( ونفخ في الصور ، فصعق من في السموات ، ومن في الأرض إلا من شاء الله . ثم نفخ فيه أخرى . فإذا هم قيام ينظرون )
وسمعت أن بعض الفلاسفة كان يقول : ( المراد من عزرائيل : النفس الكلية لفلك و زحل . وأما أتباع عزرائيل فهي النفوس المتشعبة من تلك النفس السارية آثارها في هذا العالم الجسماني . وأما إسرافيل فهو : النفس الكلية لفلك و الشمس » والدليل عليه : أن ثبت أن الإسرافيل ثلاثة أنواع من نفخ الصور وهي نفخة
And among the great angels are Israfeel and Azrael, peace be upon them. Many reports indicate them. It is established in the reports that Azrael is the Angel of Death. He Exalted said: (Say, the Angel of Death will take you away). And he must have branches, results, and helpers. As He Exalted said: (Until when death comes to one of you, Our messengers take him, and they do not fail). And He Exalted said: (And if you could see when the angels take the souls of those who disbelieve, striking their faces and their backs). As for Israfeel, peace be upon him, reports indicate that he is the master of the trumpet, as He said: (And the trumpet is blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth will fall unconscious except whom Allah wills. Then it is blown again, and behold, they are standing, looking). And I heard that some of the philosophers used to say: 'The meaning of Azrael is the universal soul of the sphere of Saturn. As for the followers of Azrael, they are the souls branching from that soul, whose effects permeate this corporeal world. As for Israfeel, he is the universal soul of the sphere of the sun.' The evidence for that: it is established that Israfeel has three types of trumpet blasts, which are: a blast...
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the great angels, now focusing on Israfeel and Azrael. It first identifies Azrael as the Angel of Death, citing Quran 32:11. It then argues that Azrael must have assistants, citing 6:61 and 8:50, where plural messengers take souls. Next, Israfeel is identified as the master of the trumpet, citing 39:68. After presenting these orthodox views, the author reports a philosophical interpretation he heard: some philosophers allegorize Azrael as the universal soul of the sphere of Saturn, with his followers being the branching souls that affect the physical world. Similarly, Israfeel is the universal soul of the sphere of the sun. The philosopher supports this by claiming Israfeel has three types of trumpet blasts (the text cuts off here). The passage thus presents both the traditional scriptural understanding and a contrasting philosophical allegory, without endorsing the latter.

عزرائيل
ملك الموت

النفس الكلية
فلك زحل
فلك الشمس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophical allegory equating angels with celestial souls is the correct Islamic view.
Correction: The text merely reports this allegory without endorsement; it is not an orthodox Islamic belief.

Checkpoint
According to the reports cited in the passage, what is the function of Israfeel?
A) He takes the souls of the dead
B) He is the master of the trumpet
C) He is the universal soul of Saturn
D) He is the leader of the angels

Key Takeaway
The Quran establishes Azrael as the Angel of Death and Israfeel as the master of the trumpet, while some philosophers allegorize them as universal souls of planetary spheres.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quran says Azrael will take your soul. The philosophers say he is an abstract cosmic principle. Which do you truly believe? If you really believed an angel will personally take your soul, would you live the same way today? What is one thing you would do differently right now to prepare for that moment?
?
Israfeel will blow the trumpet, causing everything to fall unconscious. That blast could come at any moment. Does your life reflect that urgency? If you knew today was the day, what would you change? Will you wait or act now?
?
You have just read about two views of angels – one literal, one philosophical. Which view makes you more accountable? If you reduce angels to metaphors, does that make you less mindful of the Day of Judgment? Examine your heart: are you using philosophy to escape the weight of divine commands?

The Angel of Death and the Master of the Trumpet
Identifies Azrael as Angel of Death and Israfil as master of the Trumpet with Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the revealed identities of the angels Azrael and Israfil and their roles as described in the Quran and reports.

Core Idea
Azrael is the Angel of Death; Israfil will blow the Trumpet.

Before exploring philosophical reinterpretations, it is essential to know what the Quran and authentic reports tell us about two of the greatest angels. This lesson establishes the scriptural basis for the identities of Azrael, the Angel of Death, and Israfil, the master of the Trumpet. We will examine the verses that define their roles and the report that Azrael has helpers.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Note the Quranic verses cited for each angel.
2
Identify Azrael's role and proof
Find the verses that identify Azrael as the Angel of Death and those that show he has assistants.
3
Identify Israfil's role and proof
Notice how the verse (39:68) describes Israfil's function with the Trumpet.
4
Reflect on the difference
Compare the two angels: one takes souls, the other initiates the resurrection. Both are major angels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جملة أكابر الملائكة : إسرافيل وعزرائيل عليهما السلام . والأخبار الكثيرة دلت عليها . وثبت في الأخبار : أن عزرائيل هو ملك الموت . قال تعالى : ( قل يتوفـاكم ملك الموت ) (٢) ويجب أن يكون له شعب ونتائج وأعوان . كما قال تعالى : ( حتى إذا جاء أحدكم الموت . توفته رسلنا وهم لا يفرطون ) (۳) وقال تعالى : ( ولو ترى إذ يتوفى الذين كفروا . الملائكة يضربون وجوههم وأدبارهم ) (4) وأما إسرافيل عليه السلام فقد دلت الأخبار على أنه صاحب الصور ، كما قال : ( ونفخ في الصور ، فصعق من في السموات ، ومن في الأرض إلا من شاء الله . ثم نفخ فيه أخرى . فإذا هم قيام ينظرون )(٥) وسمعت (٦) أن بعض الفلاسفة كان يقول : ( المراد من عزرائيل : النفس الكلية لفلك و زحل . وأما أتباع عزرائيل فهي النفوس المتشعبة من تلك النفس السارية آثارها في هذا العالم الجسماني . وأما إسرافيل فهو : النفس الكلية لفلك و الشمس » والدليل عليه : أن ثبت أن الإسرافيل ثلاثة أنواع من نفخ الصور وهي نفخة الفزع ، ونفخة القيام ونفخة الصعق . وهذه الثلاثة حاصلة للشمس فإن عند غروبها يستولي الفزع على جميع الحيوانات ، فترجع كلها إلى أماكنها [ وعند غروب الشفق تحصل نفخة الصعق ، لأن الحيوانات بأسرها تبقى في مساكنها (۱) ] مستلقية كأنها الأموات. وعند طلوعها من المشرق تقوم الحيوانات بأسرها ، وتقوى بعد ضعفها وتصير أحياء بعد موتها :
And among the great angels are Israfil and Azrael, peace be upon them. Many reports have indicated them. And it is established in the reports that Azrael is the Angel of Death. Allah Most High said: 'Say: The Angel of Death will take you away' (32:11). And he must have subdivisions, consequences, and assistants. As Allah Most High said: 'Until when death comes to one of you, Our messengers take him, and they do not fail' (6:61). And He said: 'And if you could see when the angels take the souls of those who disbelieve, striking their faces and their backs' (8:50). As for Israfil, peace be upon him, the reports have indicated that he is the master of the Trumpet, as He said: 'And the Trumpet will be blown, and whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on earth will be stunned, except whom Allah wills. Then it will be blown another time, and behold, they will be standing, looking on' (39:68). And I heard that some of the philosophers used to say: 'The intended meaning of Azrael is the universal soul of the sphere of Saturn. And as for the followers of Azrael, they are the souls branching from that soul whose effects pervade this corporeal world. And as for Israfil, he is the universal soul of the sphere of the Sun.' And the evidence for it is that it is established that Israfil has three types of trumpet blasts: the blast of terror, the blast of resurrection, and the blast of stunning. And these three occur to the sun, for at its setting, terror seizes all animals, so they all return to their places [and at the setting of the twilight, the blast of stunning occurs, because all animals remain in their dwellings] lying down as if dead. And at its rising from the east, all animals rise, and they become strong after their weakness and become alive after their death.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage defines the two great angels Israfil and Azrael. It first identifies Azrael as the Angel of Death, supported by Quranic verses that confirm he has helpers. Then it identifies Israfil as the master of the Trumpet, with a verse describing the trumpet blasts. The author then reports a philosophical interpretation: some philosophers allegorize Azrael as the universal soul of the sphere of Saturn and Israfil as the universal soul of the sphere of the Sun. They also give an argument linking the three trumpet blasts (terror, resurrection, stunning) to the daily cycle of the sun: terror at sunset, stunning at twilight, and resurrection at sunrise. The author presents this as something he heard, not necessarily endorsing it, but highlighting the philosophical attempt to reinterpret angelology.

Key Terms
ملك الموت
صاحب الصور
نفخ الصور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Azrael is the sole taker of souls without any helpers.
Correction: The Quran and reports affirm that Azrael has messengers (rusul) who assist him in taking souls.

Checkpoint
According to the Quranic verses cited, what is the role of Azrael?
A) He blows the Trumpet.
B) He is the Angel of Death.
C) He is the universal soul of Saturn.
D) He is the keeper of Paradise.

Key Takeaway
Azrael and Israfil are established as real angels through Quranic evidence, with specific roles in death and resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage tells you that Azrael and his assistants are charged with taking every soul, including yours. If you truly believed that your next breath could be your last, what is one concrete change you would make in your daily life starting now?
?
Israfil's Trumpet will cause all to be stunned and then resurrected. If you knew with certainty that you will stand before Allah after that second blow, how would your priorities shift today?
?
The Quran states that the angels strike the faces of disbelievers at death (8:50). After reading this passage, are you certain you are not among them? What specific belief or action from this lesson can you hold onto to secure your fate?

A Philosophical Reinterpretation of Israfil and Azrael

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a philosophical reinterpretation of Israfil and Azrael as universal souls of planetary spheres and the argument based on the sun's daily cycle.

Core Idea
Some philosophers saw Azrael and Israfil as souls of Saturn and the Sun.

Having established the literal angelic identities from revelation, we now turn to an interesting philosophical interpretation that was reported by the author. Some philosophers allegorized Azrael and Israfil, turning them into cosmic principles. This lesson examines their argument that the three trumpet blasts correspond to the daily motions of the sun, offering a naturalistic explanation.

3

The Fourth Rank: Angels of Paradise and Hell
Defines the fourth rank of angels: those in charge of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth rank of angels as described in the Quran and distinguish the literal belief from the philosophical allegorization.

Core Idea
Angels of Paradise and Hell are real beings, not mere planetary souls.

We now turn to the fourth category of angels explicitly named in the Quran: those assigned to Paradise and Hell. The Quran gives vivid descriptions of both groups, and some philosophers attempted to reinterpret them allegorically. In this lesson, we examine the scriptural evidence and the philosophical alternative.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author presents the two subgroups with their supporting verses.
Pay attention to the specific attributes mentioned for each group.
2
Identify the two subgroups
The passage divides the fourth rank into angels of Paradise and angels of Hell. Find the Quranic verses cited for each and note the key qualities: welcoming peace for Paradise's angels, harshness and obedience for Hell's angels.
3
Compare the philosophical interpretation
After presenting the Quranic descriptions, the author reports a philosophical view that allegorizes these angels as the souls of Jupiter and Mars. Compare this with the literal understanding.
Reflect on why some philosophers might have proposed such an allegory.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you grasp the Quranic description of Hell's angels. Then consider the activity to reinforce the lesson.

And the fourth rank of the angels mentioned in the Quran: the angels of Paradise and the angels of Hell. As for the angels of Paradise, His saying: 'And the angels enter upon them from every gate, “Peace be upon you for what you patiently endured.” And excellent is the final home' (13:23-24). And as for the angels of Hell, His saying: 'Over it are angels, harsh and severe; they do not disobey Allah in what He commands them, but they do what they are commanded' (66:6). And some of the philosophers used to say: 'The intended meaning of the angels of Paradise is the souls of the sphere of Jupiter, and the intended meaning of the angels of Hell is the souls of the sphere of Mars.'

Commentary

The author then reports a philosophical interpretation that allegorizes these angels as the souls of the spheres of Jupiter (for Paradise) and Mars (for Hell). Again, the philosophical view is presented alongside the literal Quranic description.

The Fifth Rank: Guardian Angels Over Humans
Enumerates the fifth rank of angels and contrasts it with a philosophical reinterpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth rank of angels as guardian angels appointed over humans, supported by Quranic evidence, and how some philosophers reinterpreted them as the 'complete nature' of human souls.

Core Idea
Angels guard humans by Allah's command—philosophers reinterpret them as natural forces.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the fifth rank of angels: those assigned to protect and record the deeds of human beings. He cites two key Quranic verses that describe angels sitting on the right and left and guarding from before and behind. He then notes that some philosophers replaced these angels with the concept of the 'complete nature,' a natural force that protects or harms souls. This contrast highlights the difference between literal revelation and philosophical interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the two Quranic verses cited.
The passage begins with 'والمرتبة الخامسة : من الملائكة : الموكلون ببني آدم'.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
The passage quotes two verses. Find where the angels are described: one verse mentions angels on the right and left 'قعيد', and the other mentions 'معقبات' guarding from before and behind. Write down the meanings.
The first verse is 50:17, the second is 13:11.
3
Examine the philosophical reinterpretation
The passage reports that some philosophers identified these guardian angels with the 'complete nature' (الطباع التام) of human souls. They claimed these spirits protect, while their opposites harm. Reflect on how this differs from the literal angelic beings.
This is a sectarian discussion; the author presents the philosophical view without necessarily endorsing it.
4
Compare the two perspectives
Compare the Quranic view (angels as created beings assigned by Allah) with the philosophical view (natural forces inherent in souls). Ask yourself which aligns with Islamic theology.
The passage does not resolve this; it simply juxtaposes them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرتبة الخامسة : من الملائكة : الموكلون ببني آدم . لقوله تعالى : ( عن اليمين وعن الشمال قعيد ) (٤) وقوله : ( له معقبات من بين يديه ومن يحفظونه من أمر الله ) (٥) وقال بعض الفلاسفة : ( قد سبق تفسير الطباع التام لكل طائفة من طوائف النفوس البشرية . فتلك الأرواح المسماة بالطباع التام : هي التي تحفظها عن الآفات والمخافات. وأما أضداد تلك الجواهر المسماة بالطباع التام ، فهي التي تلقيها في المعاطب والمهالك ) .
And the fifth rank: of the angels: those appointed over the children of Adam. According to His saying: 'On the right and on the left, sitting' (50:17) and His saying: 'For him are successive [angels] before him and behind him, guarding him by the command of Allah' (13:11). And some of the philosophers said: 'The interpretation of the complete nature for each group of human souls has already preceded. So those spirits called the complete nature are the ones that guard them against afflictions and fears. And as for the opposites of those substances called the complete nature, they are the ones that cast them into disasters and destructions.'
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth rank of angels: those appointed over human beings as guardians. It cites two Quranic verses: one mentioning the two recording angels on the right and left, and another mentioning the successive angels who guard a person from before and behind by Allah's command. The author then reports a philosophical reinterpretation: these guardian angels are identified with the 'complete nature' of human souls, which protects them from harm, while their opposites cause harm. Again, the philosophical view is juxtaposed with the literal Quranic statements.

Key Terms
معقبات
الطباع التام
قعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the angels over humans are only recording angels.
Correction: The Quran also mentions 'معقبات' which guard humans from before and behind (13:11).

Checkpoint
What Quranic evidence is provided for the angels that guard humans?
A) 'Over it are angels, harsh and severe.'
B) 'On the right and on the left, sitting.'
C) 'He is the universal soul of the sphere of the Sun.'
D) 'The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it.'

Key Takeaway
The fifth rank of angels consists of those appointed over humans as guardians, as attested by the Quran, though some philosophers reinterpret them as natural forces.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live with the constant awareness that angels are recording your every word and deed? How would your actions change if you truly felt their presence today?
?
Have you ever reduced the reality of angels to mere metaphors or natural forces, like the philosophers in this passage? What does that reveal about your faith in the unseen?
?
If Allah has appointed angels to guard you by His command, what does that demand from you in terms of gratitude and obedience? Will you thank Him today and act accordingly?

Angels Appointed Over the Sons of Adam
The fifth rank of angels as protectors of humans, with Qur'anic and philosophical statements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth rank of angels as guardians over humans, the Qur'anic evidence, and the philosophical reinterpretation of these angels as 'perfect natures'.

Core Idea
Angels guard and record deeds by Allah's command; philosophers call them 'perfect natures'.

This passage introduces the fifth rank of angels—those appointed over the sons of Adam. The author grounds this in two clear Qur'anic verses, then reports a philosophical reinterpretation that identifies these angels with 'perfect natures' of human souls. Understanding this contrast helps clarify the Islamic doctrine of guardian angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall flow. Note that the author presents two distinct views: the Qur'anic and the philosophical.
2
Identify the two Qur'anic proofs
Find the two verses cited. The first (Surah Qaf 50:17) mentions angels sitting on the right and left. The second (Surah ar-Ra'd 13:11) mentions successive angels protecting humans by Allah's command.
These verses establish the literal existence of guardian angels.
3
Understand the philosophical reinterpretation
Read the philosophers' statement. They reinterpret the angels as 'perfect natures'—spirits that protect humans, with opposites that lead to destruction.
The author reports this as a secondary opinion, not necessarily endorsing it.
4
Compare the two views
Contrast the direct Qur'anic teaching with the allegorical philosophical reading. Reflect on why the author includes both.
This highlights the difference between literal and metaphorical interpretations.

والمرتبة الخامسة : من الملائكة : الموكلون ببني آدم . لقوله تعالى : ( عن اليمين وعن الشمال قعيد ) (٤) وقوله : ( له معقبات من بين يديه ومن يحفظونه من أمر الله ) (٥) وقال بعض الفلاسفة : ( قد سبق تفسير الطباع التام لكل طائفة من طوائف النفوس البشرية . فتلك الأرواح المسماة بالطباع التام : هي التي تحفظها عن الآفات والمخافات. وأما أضداد تلك الجواهر المسماة بالطباع التام ، فهي التي تلقيها في المعاطب والمهالك ) .
And the fifth rank of the angels: those appointed over the sons of Adam. According to His saying, the Most High: 'On the right and on the left, sitting.' (4) And His saying: 'For him are successive [angels] before him and behind him, protecting him by the command of Allah.' (5) And some philosophers said: 'The interpretation of the perfect nature for each group of the classes of human souls has preceded. So those spirits called the perfect nature are those that protect them from harms and fears. And as for the opposites of those substances called the perfect nature, they are those that cast them into disasters and destructions.'
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth rank of angels as those appointed specifically to guard and record the deeds of human beings. The author provides two Qur'anic proofs: the first (Surah Qaf, verse 17) mentions angels sitting on the right and left to record deeds; the second (Surah ar-Ra'd, verse 11) describes 'mu'aqqibat' (successive angels) protecting humans by Allah's command. He then reports a philosophical interpretation that reinterprets these angels as 'perfect natures' (taba'i' tamm) of human souls—the spirits that preserve humans from harm, while their opposites lead to destruction. The passage thus presents both the literal Qur'anic view and an allegorical philosophical reading.

The Sixth Rank of Angels: Literal Meaning of the Oaths
Author defines the sixth rank of angels and explains the literal meaning of 'الصافات'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the sixth rank of angels and the literal interpretation of the Qur'anic oath 'الصافات' as holy spirits standing in awe of Allah.

Core Idea
The angels at the world's extremities are holy spirits lined in ranks before Allah.

Sanusi introduces the sixth rank of angels, those appointed at the extremities of the world, and cites a Qur'anic oath from Surah as-Saffat. The passage first offers a straightforward understanding of the 'saffat' as holy spirits in the station of divine majesty. This lesson focuses on that literal meaning before considering alternative interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage defining the sixth rank
Read the Arabic passage defining the sixth rank and the literal interpretation of 'الصافات صفا'. Notice the description of the spirits standing upon ordered degrees.
2
Identify the key terms from the verse
Note the terms 'الصافات', 'الزاجرات', 'التاليات' and the phrase 'الأرواح المقدسة' (holy spirits).
3
Understand the literal meaning of 'saffat'
The author says the 'saffat' are holy spirits standing in awe of Allah, arranged in degrees and different ranks. This is the basic interpretation.
4
Reflect on the rank's role
Consider that these angels are stationed at the extremities (atraf) of this world, indicating their function in the cosmic order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمرتبة السادسة : الملائكة الموكلون بأطراف هذا العالم . قال الله تعالى : والصافات صفا . فالزاجرات زجراً . فالتاليات ذكراً ) (1) فالمراد بقوله : الصافات صفا : الأرواح المقدسة الواقفة في مقام الهيبة والجلال على درجات مرتبة ، ومراتب مختلفة . وقال بعض الفلاسفة : المراد بقوله : « والصافات صفاً ، أرواح فلك ه الشمس ، لأن الشمس سلطان عالم الجسمانيات ، وروحها أعظم الأرواح وأما أرواح سائر الأفلاك ، فإنها عبيده وخدمه . وكأنها واقفة عنده صفاً صفاً وقوله : ( فالزاجرات زجراً ) هو أرواح فلك المريخ ) ] وقوله : ( فالتاليات ذكراً ) هو أرواح فلك و المشتري ، وكذا قوله : ( والذاريات ذروا ) (۳) إلى قوله : ( فالمقسمات أمراً ) وقوله : ( والنازعات غرقاً ) (۳) إلى قوله : ( فالمديرات أمراً ) والكلام المستقصى في تفسير هذه الآيات مذكور في ( التفسير الكبير )
And the sixth rank: the angels appointed at the extremities of this world. Allah the Most High said: 'And those who line up in ranks, and those who drive away, and those who recite the Reminder.' (1) So what is meant by His saying: 'Those who line up in ranks' is the holy spirits standing in the station of awe and majesty upon ordered degrees and different ranks. And some philosophers said: 'What is meant by His saying: “And those who line up in ranks” are the spirits of the sphere of the sun, because the sun is the sovereign of the physical world, and its spirit is the greatest of spirits. As for the spirits of the other spheres, they are its slaves and servants, and they appear standing before it rank after rank.' And His saying: 'Those who drive away' is the spirits of the sphere of Mars. And His saying: 'Those who recite the Reminder' is the spirits of the sphere of Jupiter. And likewise His saying: 'And those who scatter' (3) up to His saying: 'And those who distribute by command.' And His saying: 'And those who tear out' (3) up to His saying: 'And those who direct affairs.' The detailed discussion on the interpretation of these verses is mentioned in 'al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage defines the sixth rank of angels as those appointed at the extremities (atraf) of this world, citing the Qur'anic oaths from Surah as-Saffat: 'And those who line up in ranks, and those who drive away, and those who recite the Reminder.' The author first gives a literal interpretation: the 'saffat' are holy spirits standing in awe before Allah. Then he reports a philosophical interpretation that identifies these angelic groups with planetary spirits: the 'saffat' (liners) are spirits of the sphere of the Sun, the 'zajirat' (drivers) are spirits of Mars, and the 'taliyat' (reciters) are spirits of Jupiter. He also references other similar oath passages from Surah adh-Dhariyat and Surah an-Nazi'at, noting that the full exegesis is found in his larger commentary 'al-Tafsir al-Kabir'. The passage thus presents a cosmological allegorical reading of these Qur'anic oaths.

الصافات
الزاجرات
التاليات
الأرواح المقدسة
أطراف العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That these angels are physical beings with wings lining up in a literal row.
Correction: The text describes them as 'الأرواح المقدسة' (holy spirits), emphasizing their spiritual nature. They stand in the station of divine majesty, not a physical line.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The sixth rank of angels are holy spirits stationed at the world's edges, standing before Allah in awe and ordered ranks.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the angels are arranged in different ranks before Allah, what does that say about the order and discipline in your own life? What area of your life lacks the 'صف' (rank) that these angels exemplify?

Philosophical Interpretation: Angels as Planetary Spirits
Author reports a philosophical interpretation linking angels to planetary spirits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical interpretation that identifies the angels mentioned in the Qur'anic oaths with the spirits of planetary spheres, particularly the Sun, Mars, and Jupiter.

Core Idea
Some philosophers see the 'saffat' as spirits of the sun sphere, the 'zajirat' as Mars, and the 'taliyat' as Jupiter.

After presenting the literal meaning, Sanusi reports an alternative interpretation attributed to 'some philosophers'. This reading connects the angelic groups from Surah as-Saffat to specific planetary spirits, placing the sun at the center of the celestial hierarchy. The lesson examines this cosmological allegory and its implications.

3
Understand the sun's central role
Notice that the sun's spirit is considered the greatest, with other sphere spirits as servants standing before it.
4
Consider the broader context
The author references other oath passages from Surah adh-Dhariyat and an-Nazi'at, and mentions his larger commentary for detailed explanation.
5
Reflect on the attribution
Recognize that this is a philosophical view, not the author's own, as indicated by 'بعض الفلاسفة'.

Three Attributes of Angels
Author enumerates three angelic attributes with Qur'anic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three attributes of angels mentioned by the author: their role as messengers, their non-spatial closeness to Allah, and the description of their obedience, each supported by Qur'anic evidence.

Core Idea
Angels' closeness to Allah is closeness in rank, not in space.

The author now turns to discuss the specific attributes (sifāt) of angels. He enumerates three key qualities: they are messengers of Allah, they are close to Him in rank, and they are obedient. Each attribute is grounded in a Qur'anic verse, showing that knowledge of the unseen world comes through divine revelation. Pay attention to how the author clarifies the nature of angelic closeness—a point often misunderstood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without stopping. Let the structure of three aspects (وجوه) become clear. Then read the translation to ensure you grasp the basic meaning.
The passage is about attributes of angels only.
2
Identify the first attribute
Find where the author states that angels are messengers of Allah. Note the Qur'anic proof cited. Ask yourself: What does 'messenger' imply about their role?
The verse is from Surah Fatir, 35:1.
3
Examine the second attribute closely
The author says angels are close to Allah. Read his explanation carefully: he explicitly denies spatial closeness. Why must closeness be in degree and rank? Reflect on the implications for our understanding of Allah's transcendence.
This is the key theological point of the lesson.
4
Note the third attribute and its two aspects
The author begins describing the obedience of angels. He mentions that it has two aspects, but only gives the first: the angels' own words of glorification. Try to infer what the second aspect might be from the context of the incomplete passage.
The text cuts off; later lessons may complete it.
5
Summarize the lesson in your own words
Write down the three attributes and the proof for each. Then explain why the second attribute is important for understanding the relationship between the Creator and His creation.
This step solidifies learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام في صفات الملائكة : فمن وجوه : الأول : إن الملائكة رسل الله . قال الله تعالى : ( جاعل الملائكة رسلا) (4) . الثاني : قربهم من الله تعالى ، قال تعالى : ( ومن عنده لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ) (٥) وليس هذا القرب بالمكان ، فلم يبق إلا أن يكون القرب بالدرجة والرتبة . الثالث : وصف طاعاتهم ، وهو من وجهين : أحدهما : قوله تعالى : حكاية عن الملائكة ونحن نسبح بحمدك
And as for the discussion on the attributes of the angels: it is from several aspects. The first: that the angels are the messengers of Allah. Allah the Most High said: 'Who made the angels messengers.' (4) The second: their closeness to Allah, the Most High. He said: 'Those who are with Him are not arrogant in His worship.' (5) And this closeness is not spatial, so nothing remains except that it is closeness in degree and rank. The third: the description of their obedience, and it is from two aspects. The first of them: His saying, the Most High, narrating from the angels: 'And we glorify You with praise'.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the attributes (sifat) of angels, listing three aspects. The first attribute is that angels are messengers (rusul) of Allah, citing the Qur'anic verse 'Who made the angels messengers' (Surah Fatir, verse 1). The second attribute is their closeness (qurb) to Allah, supported by the verse 'Those who are with Him are not arrogant in His worship' (Surah al-Anbiya, verse 19). The author clarifies that this closeness is not spatial but rather in degree and rank. The third attribute concerns the description of their obedience (ta'at), which the author says has two aspects. He begins the first aspect by quoting the Qur'anic verse where the angels say, 'And we glorify You with praise' (from Surah al-Baqarah, verse 30, though incomplete here). The passage cuts off before completing the second aspect or the full third attribute. The discussion is presented as an enumeration with Qur'anic proofs.

رسل الله
القرب بالدرجة والرتبة
طاعاتهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the closeness of angels to Allah is spatial, like being physically near Him.
Correction: The author explicitly rejects spatial closeness by saying 'وليس هذا القرب بالمكان' (and this closeness is not spatial), and clarifies it is closeness in degree and rank.

Checkpoint

B) It is closeness in degree and rank
C) It is metaphorical only

Key Takeaway
Angels have three key attributes: they are messengers, they are close to Allah in rank (not spatially), and they are obedient, as evidenced by Qur'anic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Angels are messengers of Allah. If your life were a message, what would it say? Is there a contradiction between what you profess and how you live? What is one step you can take this week to align your actions with the message of Islam?

Interpreting the Angels in Surat al-Saffat
The author presents a philosophical interpretation of Quranic verses describing angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi presents both a literal and a philosophical interpretation of the angelic descriptions in Surat al-Saffat.

Core Idea
Quranic angels are interpreted as celestial sphere spirits in philosophical exegesis.

Al-Razi introduces a dual interpretation of the Quranic verses that describe angels as rows, drivers, reciters, etc. He first gives a straightforward reading: these are holy spirits standing in awe before God. Then he presents a philosophical view that identifies these spirits with the souls of the celestial spheres, each associated with a specific planet. This passage shows the intersection of Islamic theology and Neoplatonic cosmology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic text and its literal translation to grasp the author’s original wording and structure.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Notice that al-Razi first gives a general meaning, then reports a specific philosophical view. Distinguish between the literal and the philosophical readings.
3
Reflect on the cosmic framework
Consider how the philosophical interpretation maps Quranic terms to celestial spheres (sun, Mars, Jupiter, etc.). Ask why a philosopher might make this connection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصافات صفا : : الأرواح المقدسة الواقفة في مقام الهيبة والجلال على درجات مرتبة ، ومراتب مختلفة
وقال بعض الفلاسفة : المراد بقوله : « والصافات صفاً » أرواح فلك الشمس ، لأن الشمس سلطان عالم الجسمانيات ، وروحها أعظم الأرواح وأما أرواح سائر الأفلاك ، فإنها عبيده وخدمه . وكأنها واقفة عنده صفاً صفاً وقوله : ( فالزاجرات زجراً ) هو أرواح فلك المريخ ) ] وقوله : ( فالتاليات ذكراً ) هو أرواح فلك المشتري ، وكذا قوله : ( والذاريات ذروا ) (۳) إلى قوله : ( فالمقسمات أمراً )
وقوله : ( والنازعات غرقاً ) (۳) إلى قوله : ( فالمديرات أمراً ) والكلام المستقصى في تفسير هذه الآيات مذكور في ( التفسير الكبير )
The Rows in Rows: the holy spirits standing in the station of majesty and awe upon arranged degrees and different ranks. And some philosophers said: what is meant by His saying 'And the rows in rows' is the spirit of the sphere of the sun, because the sun is the sovereign of the physical world, and its spirit is the greatest of spirits. As for the spirits of the other spheres, they are its servants and attendants; it is as if they are standing before it row after row. And His saying: 'And the drivers driving' are the spirits of the sphere of Mars. And His saying: 'And the reciters reciting' are the spirits of the sphere of Jupiter. Likewise His saying: 'And the scatterers scattering' up to His saying: 'and the distributors of the command'. And His saying: 'And the pluckers plunging' up to His saying: 'and the managers of the command'. And the detailed discussion on the interpretation of these verses is mentioned in 'al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage presents an interpretation of several Quranic verses that describe angels (الصافات, الزاجرات, التاليات, الذاريات, النازعات). The author first gives a literal interpretation: the 'rows in rows' refer to the holy spirits standing in awe before God. He then reports a philosophical interpretation that identifies these spirits with the souls of the celestial spheres: the spirit of the sun corresponds to the rows, the spirit of Mars to the drivers, the spirit of Jupiter to the reciters, and so on. The passage concludes by referring readers to al-Razi's al-Tafsir al-Kabir for a more detailed exegesis.

Key Terms
الصافات
الزاجرات
التاليات
الذاريات
النازعات
أرواح الأفلاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophical interpretation is the only meaning intended by the Quranic verses.
Correction: Al-Razi presents the philosophical view as one interpretation ('قال بعض الفلاسفة') and also gives a literal interpretation, indicating it is not the sole meaning.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophical interpretation mentioned, what does 'والصافات صفاً' refer to?
A) The souls of the sphere of Mars
B) The souls of the sphere of Jupiter
C) The souls of the sphere of the sun
D) The souls of all spheres collectively

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi presents a philosophical exegesis that identifies the angels in Surat al-Saffat with the spirits of celestial spheres, linking Quranic imagery to Neoplatonic cosmology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you stand in prayer, do you imagine yourself among the rows of angels standing in awe before Allah, or has the prayer become a thoughtless habit? What specific change will you make today to stand with true reverence?
?
The philosophers reinterpreted the Quran to fit Aristotelian cosmology. Are there any beliefs or ideas from the world around you that you unknowingly use to reinterpret the Quran today? How can you guard against that?
?
If you were to choose only one interpretation of these verses—the literal angels standing in awe or the philosophical celestial spirits—which would you base your faith on? What does that choice reveal about your attachment to Allah versus attachment to human philosophy?

First Three Attributes of Angels
Enumerates first three attributes of angels with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first three attributes of angels—messengership, proximity, and obedience—as derived from the Quran.

Core Idea
Angels are defined by their roles as messengers, their rank-based proximity to God, and their perfect obedience.

The author begins a systematic discussion of angelic attributes by listing the first three. Each attribute is grounded in explicit Quranic verses, demonstrating that our knowledge of angels comes from revelation. This passage shows how the Qur'an describes angels not only as messengers but also as beings of high status and total submission to God's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with translation
Read the Arabic and translation to get the flow. Note how each attribute is introduced with 'the first', 'the second', etc.
Pay attention to the structure: three main attributes, the third with two sub-aspects.
2
Identify each attribute and its Quranic proof
Find the three attributes and the verses cited. Notice that the third attribute has two sub-aspects: glorification and obedience by command.
3
Reflect on the clarification about proximity
The author explicitly says proximity is not spatial but by rank. This is a key point to avoid misunderstanding.
This clarifies that angelic proximity is about honor and station, not physical location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام في صفات الملائكة : 
فمن وجوه :
الأول : إن الملائكة رسل الله . قال الله تعالى : ( جاعل الملائكة رسلا ) (4) .
الثاني : قربهم من الله تعالى ، قال تعالى : ( ومن عنده لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ) (٥) وليس هذا القرب بالمكان ، فلم يبق إلا أن يكون القرب بالدرجة والرتبة .
الثالث : وصف طاعاتهم ، وهو من وجهين :
أحدهما : قوله تعالى حكاية عن الملائكة : ( ونحن نسبح بحمدك ونقدس لك ) (۱) وقال تعالى في آيتين أخريين : ( وإنا لنحن الصافون . وإنا لنحن المسبحون ) (٢)

The second: their proximity to God Almighty. He said: 'And those who are with Him do not disdain to worship Him' (Q. 21:19). The third: description of their acts of obedience, and it is from two aspects: one of them: His statement, relating from the angels: 'And we glorify Your praise and sanctify You' (Q. 2:30). And He said: 'They do not outstrip Him in speech, and they act by His command' (Q. 21:27).

Commentary
This passage lists the first three attributes of angels as part of a systematic discussion. The first attribute is that angels are messengers (رسل) of God, citing Q. 35:1. The second is their proximity (قرب) to God, which is not physical but in rank, based on Q. 21:19. The third is the description of their acts of obedience (طاعاتهم), which has two aspects: first, their glorification and sanctification of God (Q. 2:30 and 37:165-166); second, their complete submission to God's command, never acting independently (Q. 19:64 and 21:27). Each attribute is supported by explicit Quranic verses.

Fourth Attribute of Angels: Their Power and Bearing the Throne
The author states the fourth attribute and provides Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective

Angels possess power beyond imagination, as they bear the Throne and manage the cosmos.

The author now turns to the fourth attribute of angels: their power. He argues that the very fact that angels manage the vast celestial bodies is clear evidence of their immense capability.
