The Fear of Angels: A Philosophical Explanation
The author describes the fifth attribute of angels: their fear of God, with a philosophical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth attribute of angels (their fear of God) and the author's philosophical explanation that their fear arises from their awareness of their own contingency.

Core Idea
Angels fear God because they know their own contingency.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah describes the fifth attribute of angels: their profound fear of God, despite their purity and innocence. The author supports this with three Quranic verses and then offers a philosophical interpretation linking their fear to their awareness of being contingent beings. Understanding this helps appreciate how Islamic theology integrates scripture with rational reflection on existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly, then its English translation. Notice the Quranic verses cited and the author's own comment beginning with 'And I say'.
The author's philosophical interpretation is distinct from the verses.
2
Identify the three Quranic verses
Find the three verses the author uses to prove that angels fear God. Think about why these verses are relevant.
The verses are Q. 16:50, Q. 21:28, and Q. 34:23.
3
Understand the philosophical interpretation
The author says the angels' fear is due to their recognition of their own possibility of existence and non-existence. Contingency in itself is non-existence. Their fear is the awareness of their fragility.
This is a key point: fear comes from awareness of contingency.
4
Reflect on the resolution
The angels become 'necessary through other' when God effuses His light of existence upon them, giving them security from annihilation. See how the fear is resolved not by removal but by divine gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخامس : وصف خوفهم فإنهم مع كثرة عبادتهم وشدة بعدهم عن الزلات يكونون [ خائفين (۷)] وجلين . قال تعالى : ( يخافون ربهم من فوقهم ) (۸) وقال : وهم من خشيته مشفقون ) (۹) وقال : ( حتى إذا فزع عن قلوبهم ، قالوا : ماذا قال ربكم ؟ قالوا : الحق : وهو العلي الكبير ) (١٠) وأقول : (١١) يحتمل أن يكون المراد من فزعهم الشديد : عرفانهم بكونهم موصوفين بإمكان الوجود والعدم . والإمكان إذا اعتبر من حيث [ هو هو (١٢) ] كان عدماً . والمراد بقوله : ( قالوا : ماذا قال ربكم ؟ قالوا : الحق : فيض نور وجوده ، وإيجاده عليهم ، فيصيرون عند ذلك واجبي الوجود بغيرهم ، فيحصل الأمن عن الهلاك والعدم (۱۳)
And the fifth: description of their fear. For despite their abundant worship and strong distance from slips, they are fearful and apprehensive. God Almighty said: 'They fear their Lord above them' (Q. 16:50). And He said: 'And they are apprehensive out of fear of Him' (Q. 21:28). And He said: 'Until when fear is removed from their hearts, they say: What did your Lord say? They say: The truth, and He is the Most High, the Great' (Q. 34:23). And I say: It is possible that what is meant by their intense fear is their recognition that they are described by possibility of existence and non-existence. And possibility, if considered in itself, is non-existence. And what is meant by His saying: 'They say: The truth' is the effusion of the light of His existence and His bringing them into existence. So at that they become necessary of existence through other than themselves, and they obtain security from annihilation and non-existence. [Editor's note: The philosophical tendency dominates the author in this interpretation.]
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth attribute of angels: their fear (خوف) of God. Despite their intense worship and innocence from sins, they are fearful. The author cites three Quranic verses: Q. 16:50, Q. 21:28, and Q. 34:23. He then offers a philosophical interpretation (أقول يحتمل) of the verse about fear being removed from their hearts. He suggests that their fear arises from their awareness of their own contingency (إمكان الوجود والعدم). Contingency, in itself, is non-existence. When God effuses His light of existence upon them, they become necessary through Him and gain security from annihilation. This explanation reflects the author's inclination towards philosophical reasoning, as noted in the editor's comment.

إمكان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think angels are fearless because they are pure and sinless, or that their fear is a sign of imperfection.
Correction: The author shows that angels' fear is profound and stems from their awareness of their own contingency, not from sin or imperfection. It is a recognition of their dependence on God.

Checkpoint

A) Their sins
B) Their awareness of their own contingency
C) Their physical weakness
D) Their ignorance of God

Key Takeaway
Angels' fear of God is rooted in their awareness of their own contingent existence, and their security comes from God's effusion of existence upon them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Refuting the Claim of Adam's Superior Knowledge over Angels
Razi concedes earthly knowledge but denies heavenly knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the argument that Adam's superior knowledge entails his superiority over all angels.

Core Idea
Knowledge superiority over earthly angels does not prove superiority over heavenly angels.

Those who claim angels are superior to humans often cite Adam's knowledge of the names. Razi grants that Adam was more knowledgeable than earthly angels, but denies this applies to heavenly angels. He promises a definitive proof of the impossibility of human superiority over heavenly angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi uses a very concessive style here.
2
Identify the distinction
Razi distinguishes between 'earthly angels' and 'heavenly angels'. Find this in the text and understand the significance.
3
Understand the logical move
Razi concedes part of the opponent's argument (Adam's knowledge of earthly angels) but denies the conclusion applies to all angels. Ask yourself why this distinction matters.
The opponent assumed Adam's knowledge was universal; Razi limits it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوجه الثالث : وهو أن آدم - عليه السلام - كان أعلم من الملائكة فنقول : مسلم أنه كان أعلم من الملائكة الأرضية . فلم قلتم إنه كان أعلم من الملائكة السماوية ؟ وسنقيم البرهان اليقيني (١) على أن ذلك محال . وأما الوجه الرابع : وهو قوله : ( إن الله اصطفى آدم . ونوحاً . وآل إبراهيم . وآل عمران . على العالمين (۲) ) فنقول : يجب حمل لفظ « العالمين » على أهل الأرض ، توفيقاً بين هذه الآية وبين دلائلنا . وأما قوله : « إن عباداتهم أشق ، فيجب أن يكونوا أفضل ، فنقول مثل هذا الكلام : مثل ما إذا قيل : إن الخباز والقصاب : تحصيلهم للقوت واللباس أشق ، فوجب أن يكونوا أفضل من سلاطين المشرق والمغرب . ولما كان هذا الكلام لا يلتفت إليه العاقل . فكذا ههنا . وأيضاً : فلو فرضنا رجلاً شديد الاستعداد لحصول المرض ، بحيث يقع بأدنى سبب في الأمراض الشديدة . ورجلاً آخر ، خلق على أكمل أنواع الصحة ، وأفضل أقسام الجمال [ فهل نقول : هما فاضلان (۳) ] إلا أن الأول أفضل من الثاني ، في الصحة والجمال . لأنه إنما يحفظ صحته بتعب شديد ، وهذا ليس كذلك ؟ ولما كان هذا الكلام باطلاً ، فكذا ههنا . وأما قوله : و الانسان إذا مال إلى الشهوة ، كان أخس من البهيمة فكذلك إذا مال : إلى جانب العقل ، كان أفضل من الملك ، فنقول : أما قوله : [ إذا مال إلى جانب الشهوة ، صار أخس من البهيمة (٤) ] فهذا باطل . وعموم الآية على المبالغة في الزجر [ والله أعلم (٥) ] .
As for the third aspect: that Adam (peace be upon him) was more knowledgeable than the angels, we say: it is granted that he was more knowledgeable than the earthly angels. But why do you claim that he was more knowledgeable than the heavenly angels? And we will establish the certain proof that this is impossible. As for the fourth aspect: His statement, 'Indeed, Allah chose Adam, Noah, the family of Abraham, and the family of Imran above the worlds,' we say: the word 'worlds' must be interpreted as the people of the earth, in order to reconcile this verse with our proofs. As for his statement, 'Their worship is more difficult, so they must be superior,' we say: this statement is like when it is said: The baker and the butcher acquire food and clothing with more difficulty, so they must be superior to the kings of the East and West. Since no rational person pays attention to this statement, so here too. Also: if we suppose a man with a strong predisposition to fall ill, such that he falls into severe diseases at the slightest cause, and another man created with the most perfect health and the best kind of beauty, [would we say: they are both virtuous?] except that the first is superior to the second in health and beauty because he preserves his health with great effort, and the other does not? Since this statement is false, so here too. As for his statement: 'When man inclines to desire, he becomes lower than the beast; similarly, when he inclines to reason, he becomes superior to the angel,' we say: as for his statement, '[When he inclines to desire, he becomes lower than the beast],' this is false. And the general import of the verse is hyperbolic in deterrence. [And Allah knows best.]
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes three arguments from those who claim that angels are superior to humans. The author proceeds in a dialectical manner, addressing each objection in order. First, he takes the argument that Adam (peace be upon him) was taught the names and was therefore more knowledgeable than the angels. The author grants that Adam was more knowledgeable than the earthly angels (i.e., those on earth), but denies that this applies to the heavenly angels, promising a conclusive proof for their superiority. Second, he addresses the verse 'Indeed, Allah chose Adam, Noah, the family of Abraham, and the family of Imran above the worlds.' He argues that the term 'worlds' must be limited to the people of the earth, in order to harmonize this verse with other definitive proofs that angels are superior. Third, he refutes the claim that the difficulty of angelic worship makes them superior. He uses two analogies: first, the skilled baker and butcher, whose work is harder than that of kings, but that does not make them superior; second, a man who maintains his health through great effort is not thereby healthier than one naturally healthy. Finally, he dismisses the comparison that man is lower than beasts when inclined to desire and higher than angels when inclined to reason, stating that the first premise is false and the verse is merely hyperbolic for deterrence.

Key Terms
الملائكة الأرضية
الملائكة السماوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Adam's superior knowledge proves he is superior to all angels.
Correction: Razi shows that the argument only applies to earthly angels, not heavenly ones.

Checkpoint
What distinction does Razi make in responding to the knowledge argument?
A) He denies Adam's knowledge.
B) He distinguishes earthly and heavenly angels.
C) He argues Adam's knowledge was partial.
D) He says angels are not knowledgeable.

Key Takeaway
Razi accepts that Adam was more knowledgeable than earthly angels but denies that this proves superiority over all angels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that a small truth you know applies to all of life? In what area of your faith are you guilty of overgeneralizing your understanding, like the opponent who thought Adam's knowledge covered all angels? Will you consciously scrutinize your assumptions today?
?
Adam, despite his excellence, was limited in knowledge about heavenly matters. When it comes to your own spiritual knowledge, do you humbly accept its boundaries, or do you secretly believe you have mastered domains that are beyond you? What would change if you admitted your limits?
?
Razi's argument forces you to distinguish between earthly and heavenly realms. Is there a 'heavenly' matter—like the Unseen or the nature of Allah—that you have spoken about with unwarranted certainty? Repent of that presumption now and commit to only speaking from revelation.

Interpreting 'Worlds' in the Verse of Divine Choice
Razi restricts 'worlds' to earthly beings to harmonize scripture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi interprets the verse 'Allah chose Adam... above the worlds' to harmonize it with the superiority of angels.

Core Idea
The term 'worlds' in the verse refers only to the people of the earth.

Opponents of angelic superiority cite the verse where Allah chose Adam and others 'above the worlds.' Razi responds by limiting the scope of 'worlds' to earthly beings, thus reconciling the verse with other proofs of angelic superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Razi's response
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the verse quoted and Razi's immediate response.
2
Understand the need for reconciliation
Razi uses a principle of tawfiq (reconciliation) between conflicting evidences. Understand why he thinks the general term must be restricted.
The term 'worlds' appears general, but other proofs show angels are superior.
3
Examine the interpretative move
Razi restricts 'worlds' to 'the people of the earth'. Ask: is there textual support for this? How does this preserve the verse's validity?
This is a common hermeneutical technique in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوجه الثالث : وهو أن آدم - عليه السلام - كان أعلم من الملائكة فنقول : مسلم أنه كان أعلم من الملائكة الأرضية . فلم قلتم إنه كان أعلم من الملائكة السماوية ؟ وسنقيم البرهان اليقيني (١) على أن ذلك محال . وأما الوجه الرابع : وهو قوله : ( إن الله اصطفى آدم . ونوحاً . وآل إبراهيم . وآل عمران . على العالمين (۲) ) فنقول : يجب حمل لفظ « العالمين » على أهل الأرض ، توفيقاً بين هذه الآية وبين دلائلنا . وأما قوله : « إن عباداتهم أشق ، فيجب أن يكونوا أفضل ، فنقول مثل هذا الكلام : مثل ما إذا قيل : إن الخباز والقصاب : تحصيلهم للقوت واللباس أشق ، فوجب أن يكونوا أفضل من سلاطين المشرق والمغرب . ولما كان هذا الكلام لا يلتفت إليه العاقل . فكذا ههنا . وأيضاً : فلو فرضنا رجلاً شديد الاستعداد لحصول المرض ، بحيث يقع بأدنى سبب في الأمراض الشديدة . ورجلاً آخر ، خلق على أكمل أنواع الصحة ، وأفضل أقسام الجمال [ فهل نقول : هما فاضلان (۳) ] إلا أن الأول أفضل من الثاني ، في الصحة والجمال . لأنه إنما يحفظ صحته بتعب شديد ، وهذا ليس كذلك ؟ ولما كان هذا الكلام باطلاً ، فكذا ههنا . وأما قوله : و الانسان إذا مال إلى الشهوة ، كان أخس من البهيمة فكذلك إذا مال : إلى جانب العقل ، كان أفضل من الملك ، فنقول : أما قوله : [ إذا مال إلى جانب الشهوة ، صار أخس من البهيمة (٤) ] فهذا باطل . وعموم الآية على المبالغة في الزجر [ والله أعلم (٥) ] .
As for the third aspect: that Adam (peace be upon him) was more knowledgeable than the angels, we say: it is granted that he was more knowledgeable than the earthly angels. But why do you claim that he was more knowledgeable than the heavenly angels? And we will establish the certain proof that this is impossible. As for the fourth aspect: His statement, 'Indeed, Allah chose Adam, Noah, the family of Abraham, and the family of Imran above the worlds,' we say: the word 'worlds' must be interpreted as the people of the earth, in order to reconcile this verse with our proofs. As for his statement, 'Their worship is more difficult, so they must be superior,' we say: this statement is like when it is said: The baker and the butcher acquire food and clothing with more difficulty, so they must be superior to the kings of the East and West. Since no rational person pays attention to this statement, so here too. Also: if we suppose a man with a strong predisposition to fall ill, such that he falls into severe diseases at the slightest cause, and another man created with the most perfect health and the best kind of beauty, [would we say: they are both virtuous?] except that the first is superior to the second in health and beauty because he preserves his health with great effort, and the other does not? Since this statement is false, so here too. As for his statement: 'When man inclines to desire, he becomes lower than the beast; similarly, when he inclines to reason, he becomes superior to the angel,' we say: as for his statement, '[When he inclines to desire, he becomes lower than the beast],' this is false. And the general import of the verse is hyperbolic in deterrence. [And Allah knows best.]
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes three arguments from those who claim that angels are superior to humans. The author proceeds in a dialectical manner, addressing each objection in order. First, he takes the argument that Adam (peace be upon him) was taught the names and was therefore more knowledgeable than the angels. The author grants that Adam was more knowledgeable than the earthly angels (i.e., those on earth), but denies that this applies to the heavenly angels, promising a conclusive proof for their superiority. Second, he addresses the verse 'Indeed, Allah chose Adam, Noah, the family of Abraham, and the family of Imran above the worlds.' He argues that the term 'worlds' must be limited to the people of the earth, in order to harmonize this verse with other definitive proofs that angels are superior. Third, he refutes the claim that the difficulty of angelic worship makes them superior. He uses two analogies: first, the skilled baker and butcher, whose work is harder than that of kings, but that does not make them superior; second, a man who maintains his health through great effort is not thereby healthier than one naturally healthy. Finally, he dismisses the comparison that man is lower than beasts when inclined to desire and higher than angels when inclined to reason, stating that the first premise is false and the verse is merely hyperbolic for deterrence.

Key Terms
العالمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Razi reconcile the verse about Adam being chosen above the worlds with the superiority of angels?
A) He says the verse is abrogated.
B) He interprets 'worlds' as the people of the earth.
C) He argues the verse refers only to Adam's descendants.
D) He says the verse is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
Razi restricts the general term 'worlds' to earthly beings to harmonize scripture with rational proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse that seems to contradict other clear proofs, do you immediately dismiss the proofs or do you seek reconciliation like Razi? What does your instinct reveal about your intellectual honesty and trust in the consistency of revelation? Will you commit to harmonizing all evidence before forming a conclusion?
?
Are you willing to accept that a verse which appears to elevate humans above angels actually refers only to people of the earth? What does this teach you about your own tendency to take verses out of context, and how can you guard against that in your daily reading of the Quran?
?
How often do you let your assumptions about a verse's meaning override the need to study it in light of the whole Quran and sound reason? What would it cost you to adopt a more rigorous approach, and are you ready to pay that price for the sake of truth?

Refuting the Argument from Difficulty of Worship
Razi uses analogical refutation against difficulty-based superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi rejects the claim that the greater difficulty of angelic worship proves their superiority.

Core Idea
Difficulty of work does not imply superiority, as shown by analogies from daily life.

Some argue that angels are superior because their worship is more difficult. Razi counters with two analogies: the baker who works harder than a king, and the sickly man who preserves health with greater effort. Neither becomes superior through difficulty.

Guided Path
1
Read the two analogies
Read the passage carefully. Identify the two analogies: the baker/butcher and the healthy/sickly man.
Notice Razi uses 'mithl' (example) to draw parallels.
2
Analyze the logical flaw
Razi points out that the opponent's reasoning is invalid: difficulty does not entail superiority. See how each analogy demonstrates this.
3
Apply to the original argument
Razi concludes 'so here too' for each analogy, applying the same reasoning to angelic worship. Understand why the analogy fits.
The argument is refuted by showing its absurdity in parallel cases.

As for the third aspect: that Adam (peace be upon him) was more knowledgeable than the angels, we say: it is granted that he was more knowledgeable than the earthly angels. But why do you claim that he was more knowledgeable than the heavenly angels? And we will establish the certain proof that this is impossible. As for the fourth aspect: His statement, 'Indeed, Allah chose Adam, Noah, the family of Abraham, and the family of Imran above the worlds,' we say: the word 'worlds' must be interpreted as the people of the earth, in order to reconcile this verse with our proofs. Since no rational person pays attention to this statement, so here too. Since this statement is false, so here too. As for his statement: 'When man inclines to desire, he becomes lower than the beast; similarly, when he inclines to reason, he becomes superior to the angel,' we say: as for his statement, '[When he inclines to desire, he becomes lower than the beast],' this is false. Commentary
This passage presents and refutes three arguments from those who claim that angels are superior to humans. The author proceeds in a dialectical manner, addressing each objection in order. First, he takes the argument that Adam (peace be upon him) was taught the names and was therefore more knowledgeable than the angels. Second, he addresses the verse 'Indeed, Allah chose Adam, Noah, the family of Abraham, and the family of Imran above the worlds.' He argues that the term 'worlds' must be limited to the people of the earth, in order to harmonize this verse with other definitive proofs that angels are superior. Third, he refutes the claim that the difficulty of angelic worship makes them superior. He uses two analogies: first, the skilled baker and butcher, whose work is harder than that of kings, but that does not make them superior; second, a man who maintains his health through great effort is not thereby healthier than one naturally healthy. Finally, he dismisses the comparison that man is lower than beasts when inclined to desire and higher than angels when inclined to reason, stating that the first premise is false and the verse is merely hyperbolic for deterrence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Difficulty of worship makes angels superior.
Correction: Difficulty does not imply virtue, as shown by everyday analogies.

Checkpoint

B) Hard work does not imply superiority.
C) Kings work harder than bakers.
D) Worship is not difficult.

Key Takeaway
Greater difficulty in worship does not make angels superior, just as harder work does not make a laborer superior to a king.

?

?

?

Refuting the Comparison of Man's Potential
Razi rejects the premise that man becomes lower than a beast when desiring.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi dismisses the claim that man is lower than beasts when following desire and higher than angels when following reason.

Core Idea
The premise that man becomes lower than a beast when inclined to desire is false.

The opponent argues that because man can be lower than beasts when driven by desire, he can be higher than angels when guided by reason. Razi counters that the first premise is false; the verse used is hyperbole for deterrence, not a factual statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the opponent's claim and Razi's response.
2
Identify the refutation
Razi calls the first part 'false' (bāṭil). Understand why he rejects it as a literal statement.
He says the verse is hyperbolic (mubālagha) for deterrence.
3
Consider the implication
If the first premise is false, the entire comparison collapses. Reflect on how Razi uses this to dismiss the argument.

Source Text

?

Classification of Proofs and First Scriptural Argument for Angel Superiority
Razi classifies proofs for angel superiority into scriptural and rational, then explains the first scriptural proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi classifies proofs for angel superiority and the first scriptural argument from the Quran, including the two inferential aspects drawn from the verse.

Core Idea
Angels are superior to humans, as shown by Quranic verses where Allah uses their honor to teach humility.

Razi begins a new section by formally categorizing the evidence for angel superiority into scriptural (samʿiyya) and rational (ʿaqliyya). He then unpacks the first scriptural proof, a Quranic verse about angels' devotion, explaining two key inferential aspects that highlight their elevated rank. This lesson will walk you through that classification and the reasoning behind the first argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of proofs
Start by reading the passage where Razi states that proofs are of two types: scriptural and rational. This sets the stage for the rest of the argument.
Notice the author immediately delimits the scope of the discussion.
2
Understand the first scriptural proof
Read the verse (Quran 21:19) and the two inferential aspects (wajhayn) that Razi extracts from it. The first concerns the meaning of 'withness', the second the logical structure of the argument.
The verse is quoted in full; pay attention to the key term 'indiyya.
3
Examine the analogy of the sultan
Razi gives an analogy of a sultan to illustrate why the argument only works if angels are superior. Reflect on how this analogy clarifies the reasoning.
This analogy is a classic rhetorical tool in kalam.
4
Reflect on the significance of 'withness'
The author explicitly clarifies that 'withness' does not mean physical proximity but honor and rank. This is a key doctrinal point to avoid misunderstanding.
This correction guards against anthropomorphic interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم : أن دلائل القائلين بأن الملك أفضل من البشر . نوعان : بعضها سمعية ، وبعضها عقلية . أما السمعية فوجوه : الأول : قوله تعالى : ( ومن عنده لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ، ولا يستحسرون . يسبحون الليل والنهار لا يفترون ) والاستدلال بهذه الآية من وجهين : الأول : إنه ليس المراد من هذه العندية : عندية المكان والجهة . فإنه محال . بل عندية القرب والشرف. ولما كانت هذه الآية واردة في صفة الملائكة ، علمنا : أن هذا النوع من الشرف حاصل لهم لا لغيرهم . والثاني : إنه سبحانه وتعالى احتج لعدم استكبارهم ، على أن غيرهم أولى بأن لا يستكبروا . ولو كان البشر أفضل من الملائكة لما تم هذا الاحتجاج . فإن السلطان إذا أراد أن يقرر على رعيته أنه يجب عليهم خدمته وطاعته ، فإنه يقول : الملوك لا يستكبرون عن طاعتي . فكيف هؤلاء المساكين . وبالجملة : فالمعلوم أن هذا الاستدلال لا يتم إلا بالأكمل على الأدون . ونظير هذه الآية في الدلالة على هذا المطلوب ، قوله تعالى : ( إن الذين عند ربك لا يستكبرون عن عبادته، ويسبحونه ، وله يسجدون )
Know that the proofs of those who say that the angel is superior to humans are of two types: some are scriptural, and some are rational. As for the scriptural, they are aspects: the first: His statement, 'And those who are with Him are not too proud to worship Him, nor do they grow weary. They glorify Him night and day, without flagging.' And the inference from this verse is from two aspects: the first: that what is meant by 'withness' is not the withness of place and direction—for that is impossible—but rather the withness of proximity and honor. Since this verse is about the description of the angels, we know that this type of honor belongs to them and not to others. The second: that He, exalted, argued from their lack of arrogance that others are more deserving of not being arrogant. If humans were superior to angels, this argument would not hold. For if the sultan wants to establish among his subjects that they must serve and obey him, he says: 'The kings are not too proud to obey me; so how about these poor wretches?' In short, it is known that this inference only works from the superior to the inferior. And a verse similar to this in indicating this point is His statement: 'Indeed, those who are with your Lord are not too proud to worship Him, and they glorify Him, and to Him they prostrate.'
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage begins a new section in which the author formally classifies the proofs for the superiority of angels over humans. He states that the proofs are of two kinds: scriptural (samʿiyya) and rational (ʿaqliyya). He then starts with the scriptural proofs, presenting the first one: the verse 'And those who are with Him are not too proud to worship Him...' (Quran 21:19). He explains two inferential aspects (wajhayn) from this verse. The first aspect concerns the word 'withness' (ʿindiyya). He clarifies that it does not mean physical proximity in place or direction, which is impossible for Allah, but rather the withness of honor and rank. Since the verse describes the angels, this honor belongs specifically to them. The second aspect is the argument itself: Allah uses the angels' lack of arrogance to argue that others (humans) should also not be arrogant. If humans were superior to angels, this argument would be flawed, because it would be using a lesser to prove a greater, which is the reverse. The author illustrates with an analogy: a sultan would say 'Even kings obey me, so how about these poor people?' The argument only works if the angels are superior in rank—using the superior to argue for the inferior. He then cites a similar verse (Quran 7:206 or 32:15? Actually it is from the end of Surah al-Aʿraf) as further evidence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that 'withness' (ʿindiyya) in the verse means physical nearness to Allah in place or direction.
Correction: The author clarifies that this is impossible for Allah, and it means the withness of honor and rank.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the intended meaning of 'withness' (ʿindiyya) in the verse about the angels?
A) Physical proximity in place
B) Temporal nearness
C) Proximity of honor and rank
D) Spiritual union

Key Takeaway
The first scriptural proof for angel superiority uses the Quranic description of angels' devotion and argues from their higher rank to teach humility to others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels never grow weary of worshipping Allah. When was the last time you felt tired of obeying Allah? What does your exhaustion reveal about the state of your heart? Will you commit to renewing your intention and asking Allah for stamina to worship Him without complaint?
?
If Allah chose to describe the angels with honor and proximity to Himself to teach humility to others, why do you still struggle with pride? Which area of your life are you most tempted to feel superior in, and how can you actively humble yourself today in light of the angels' example?
?
The sultan's argument uses the obedience of the noblest to rebuke the lowliest. Do you recognize that Allah has placed people in your life who are more obedient than you? Will you allow their example to shame you into sincerity, or will you resent their closeness to Allah? Make a concrete decision to learn from one such person this week.

Scriptural Proof for Angels' Superiority
The author presents the first scriptural proof for angels' superiority, with two aspects of deduction from Quran 21:19-20.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Quran 21:19-20 to argue for the superiority of angels over humans through two aspects of deduction.

Core Idea
Angels' honor is proven by their exclusive 'indiyyah and their role as models for human obedience.

The author begins the scriptural argument for angels' superiority by citing a key Quranic verse. He carefully interprets the word 'indiyyah to mean honor, not spatial proximity, and shows how the verse's logic demands that angels be higher in rank than humans.

Guided Path
1
Understand the classification of proofs
The author states that proofs for angels' superiority are of two types: scriptural and rational. He begins with scriptural, and this lesson covers the first such proof.
This sets the overall context for the argument.
2
Examine the first aspect: 'indiyyah as honor
The author argues that 'indiyyah in the verse means nearness in honor, not place. Since this description is exclusively for angels, they possess a unique honor.
This counters a potential misconception about God's location.
3
Examine the second aspect: the argument from example
God uses the angels' lack of arrogance to argue that humans, who are lower, should be even more obedient. This implies angels are the standard of perfection.
The analogy of the king and subjects clarifies the logic.
4
Recognize the supporting verse
The author cites Quran 7:206 as a parallel proof, reinforcing the same conclusion.
This shows consistency in the Quranic argument.

واعلم : أن دلائل القائلين بأن الملك أفضل من البشر . نوعان : بعضها سمعية ، وبعضها عقلية
أما السمعية فوجوه :
الأول : قوله تعالى : ( ومن عنده لا يستكبرون عن عبادته ، ولا يستحسرون . يسبحون الليل والنهار لا يفترون ) والاستدلال بهذه الآية من وجهين :
الأول : إنه ليس المراد من هذه العندية : عندية المكان والجهة . فإنه محال . بل عندية القرب والشرف. ولما كانت هذه الآية واردة في صفة الملائكة ، علمنا : أن هذا النوع من الشرف حاصل لهم لا لغيرهم .
والثاني : إنه سبحانه وتعالى احتج لعدم استكبارهم ، على أن غيرهم أولى بأن لا يستكبروا . ولو كان البشر أفضل من الملائكة لما تم هذا الاحتجاج . فإن السلطان إذا أراد أن يقرر على رعيته أنه يجب عليهم خدمته وطاعته ، فإنه يقول : الملوك لا يستكبرون عن طاعتي . فكيف هؤلاء المساكين .
وبالجملة : فالمعلوم أن هذا الاستدلال لا يتم إلا بالأكمل على الأدون . ونظير هذه الآية في الدلالة على هذا المطلوب ، قوله تعالى : ( إن الذين عند ربك لا يستكبرون عن عبادته، ويسبحونه ، وله يسجدون )
فإن قيل : الاعتراض على الوجه الأول : أن نقول : إنه تعالى أثبت هذه العندية في الآخرة لأحاد المؤمنين . وهو قوله : ( في مقعد صدق عند مليك مقتدر ) وأما في الدنيا فقال عليه السلام ، حاكياً عن الله تعالى : ( أنا عند المنكسرة قلوبهم لاجلي ، وهذا أكثر إشعاراً بالتعظيم ، لأن هذا الخبر يدل على أنه سبحانه عند هؤلاء المنكسرين . والآية التي تمسكتم بها : تدل على أن الملائكة عند الله . ولا شك أن كون الله عند العبد ، أدخل في التعظيم من كون العبد عند الله
أما الاعتراض على الوجه الثاني : فهو أن نقول : لا نزاع في أن الملائكة أشد قدرة وقوة من البشر ، ويكفي في صحة هذا الدليل : هذا القدر من التفاوت ، فإنه يقال : إن الملائكة ، مع شدة قوتهم واستيلائهم على أجرام السموات والأرض ، وأمنهم من الضعف والعجز [ والهرم والمرض وطول أعمارهم ] لا يتركون العبودية لحظة واحدة. فالبشر مع نهاية ضعفهم [ مع ما يصيبهم من الأمراض والآفات ] أولى أن لا يتمردوا . فهذا يدل على أن الملائكة أكثر قوة من البشر وهذا القدر كاف في صحة الاستدلال . ولا نزاع في حصول التفاوت في هذا المعنى ] أما لم قلتم : إن ذلك يدل على أن الملائكة أفضل من البشر ؟
والجواب عن الأول : أن نقول : إن قوله : ( أنا عند المنكسرة قلوبهم لأجلي مشعر بأن المراد بتلك العنـديـة : الحفظ والحراسة والرحمة . فإن السلطان إذا قال يا مسكين أنا معك . فهم كل أحد منه : أن المراد أن لا يهمله ولا يضيع مهمه . أما إذا قيل لبعض الأكابر أو العظماء : إنه من المقربين عنـد السلطان . فإنه يفهم منه كمال الدرجة والمنقبة. فعلم أنه لا تعلق لأحد البابين بالآخر
والجواب عن السؤال الثاني : إن الاستدلال بأفعال الملائكة إنما يتم إذا قلنا : الملائكة موصوفون بالكمال في القوة والقدرة والعلم . لأنهم لو لم يكونوا أعلم من البشر ، لم يكن فعلهم حجة على البشر لأن فعل الجاهل لا يمكن جعله حجة على العالم .
Know that the proofs of those who say that the angel is superior to man are of two types: some of them are scriptural, and some are rational. As for the scriptural, they are aspects: The first is His statement, the Most High: 'And those who are [in His presence] with Him are not arrogant in worship of Him, nor do they tire. They exalt [Him] night and day, and do not slacken.' (Quran 21:19-20) The deduction from this verse is in two aspects: The first: that what is meant by this 'indiyyah (nearness/presence) is not the nearness of place and direction, for that is impossible. Rather, it is the nearness of proximity and honor. Since this verse is revealed describing the angels, we know that this type of honor is attained by them and not by others. The second: that He, the Most High, argued for their lack of arrogance, [intending] that others are more entitled not to be arrogant. If humans were superior to angels, this argument would not be valid. For if the sultan wants to establish upon his subjects that they must serve and obey him, he says: 'The kings do not show arrogance in obeying me; how then these poor ones?' In short, it is known that this argument is only valid by [comparing] the more perfect to the lower. And similar to this verse in indicating this desired conclusion is His statement, the Most High: 'Indeed, those who are with your Lord are not arrogant toward His worship, and they exalt Him, and to Him they prostrate.' (Quran 7:206) But if it is said: The objection to the first aspect is that we say: He, the Most High, has established this 'indiyyah in the Hereafter for the individual believers, as His saying: 'In a seat of truth near a Sovereign, All-Powerful.' (Quran 54:55) And as for this world, the Prophet, peace be upon him, said, narrating from God the Most High: 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for My sake.' And this is more indicative of glorification, because this report indicates that He, the Most High, is with these broken-hearted ones. While the verse you hold indicates that the angels are with God. There is no doubt that God's being with the servant is more indicative of glorification than the servant's being with God. As for the objection to the second aspect, it is that we say: There is no dispute that the angels are more powerful and stronger than humans, and this degree of difference suffices for the validity of this proof. For it is said: The angels, despite their intense strength and domination over the celestial and terrestrial bodies, and their immunity from weakness, incapacity, [senility, illness, and length of their lives], do not abandon worship for a single moment. Humans, with their extreme weakness, [with what afflicts them of illnesses and ailments], are more entitled not to rebel. This indicates that the angels are more powerful than humans, and this degree suffices for the validity of the deduction. And there is no dispute about the existence of difference in this meaning. But why do you say that this indicates that the angels are superior to humans? The answer to the first [objection]: That we say: His statement: 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for my sake' suggests that what is meant by that 'indiyyah is protection, guardianship, and mercy. For if the sultan says, 'O poor one, I am with you,' everyone understands from it that the intent is that he will not neglect him, nor waste his important affairs. But if it is said to some great ones or nobles that they are among those close to the sultan, then from it is understood perfection of rank and honor. Thus, it is known that one of the two categories is not connected to the other. The answer to the second question: The deduction from the actions of the angels is only valid if we say that the angels are described with perfection in strength, power, and knowledge. For if they were not more knowledgeable than humans, their action would not be a proof against humans, because the action of the ignorant cannot be made a proof against the knowledgeable.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage presents the first scriptural proof for the superiority of angels over humans, followed by two objections and their answers. The author begins by classifying the proofs into two types: scriptural and rational, then immediately proceeds to the first scriptural proof: Quran 21:19-20. He explains that the verse contains two aspects of argument. The first aspect concerns the term 'indiyyah (nearness/presence), clarifying that it refers not to spatial nearness (which is impossible for God) but to nearness in honor and rank. Since this verse describes the angels, this honor is exclusive to them. The second aspect is that God uses the angels' lack of arrogance as a contrast to argue that human beings, who are lower, should be even more obedient. The author draws an analogy: if a king points to kings who obey him, his subjects, being of lesser status, should follow suit. Thus, the argument hinges on the superiority of the angels. He then mentions a parallel Quranic verse (7:206). Next, an objection is raised against the first aspect: God also uses 'indiyyah for believers, both in the Hereafter (Quran 54:55) and in this world (the hadith qudsi 'I am with those whose hearts are broken for My sake'). This close relationship with God actually implies greater honor for believers than for angels, since God being with His servant is more magnificent than the servant being with God. The author answers this by distinguishing between two meanings of 'indiyyah: when God says 'I am with you', it signifies protection, care, and mercy—like a sultan telling a poor man 'I am with you' means he will not neglect him. But when it is said that someone is 'with the sultan' or 'close to the sultan', it implies high rank and honor. Thus, the two contexts are different and do not conflict; the angelic 'indiyyah indicates honor, while the divine 'indiyyah for believers indicates mercy. The second objection is that the scriptural proof only shows that angels are physically stronger, not necessarily superior in all respects. The author responds by asserting that the argument from strength works only if angels also have perfect knowledge; otherwise, the actions of ignorant beings cannot be used as a proof against knowledgeable ones. Therefore, the angels are superior in knowledge as well, completing the proof of their overall superiority.

عنـدية
شرف
قرب
استدلال
احتجاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'indiyyah means God is in a physical place.
Correction: The author clarifies it means nearness in honor and rank, not spatial location.

Checkpoint
What two meanings of 'indiyyah does the author discuss?
A) Spatial nearness and nearness in honor
B) Nearness in time and space
C) Nearness in love and fear
D) Nearness in essence and attributes

Key Takeaway
The scriptural proof for angels' superiority rests on interpreting 'indiyyah as honor and using the angels as a model for human obedience, which presupposes their higher station.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that angels never tire of worship, do you feel a sense of shame about your own laziness in worship? What is one specific act of worship you have been neglecting, and what step will you take this week to change that?
?
The lesson shows that God uses angels as a model to shame humans into obedience. Are you someone who needs that kind of comparison to be motivated? Why do you think you are not moved by the mere command of your Lord?
?
If angels are superior in honor and obedience, what does that mean for your pride? Do you truly accept that there are creatures better than you, and how does that affect your humility before God?

Defending the Proof: Two Objections Answered
The author responds to two objections against the scriptural proof, distinguishing between types of nearness and affirming angels' knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author answers two objections to the scriptural proof for angels' superiority, distinguishing between different types of nearness and establishing angels' knowledge.

Core Idea
Scriptural proofs withstand objections by clarifying meanings and affirming that angels possess both power and knowledge.

After presenting the scriptural proof, the author anticipates two objections. The first objection challenges the interpretation of 'indiyyah, citing verses that show God's nearness to believers is actually more honorable. The second objection argues that the proof only shows angels' physical strength, not superiority in rank. The author answers both, defending the proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first objection
The objector argues that 'indiyyah is also used for believers (e.g., Quran 54:55 and hadith qudsi), and God's being with the servant is more honorable than the servant being with God.
This challenges the exclusivity of the honor.
2
Study the author's answer to the first objection
The author distinguishes between two types of 'indiyyah: when God is 'with' the servant, it means protection and mercy; when the servant is 'with' God, it means rank and honor. The two are different.
The analogy of the sultan clarifies this distinction.
3
Understand the second objection
The objector says the proof only shows angels are stronger than humans, not necessarily superior in a way that proves overall superiority.
The objector accepts physical strength difference but denies implication of full superiority.
4
Study the author's answer to the second objection
The author argues that for the angels' actions to be a valid example for humans, angels must also have perfect knowledge. Otherwise, actions of the ignorant cannot be proof for the knowledgeable.
This establishes angels' superiority in knowledge as well.

This close relationship with God actually implies greater honor for believers than for angels, since God being with His servant is more magnificent than the servant being with God. The author answers this by distinguishing between two meanings of 'indiyyah: when God says 'I am with you', it signifies protection, care, and mercy—like a sultan telling a poor man 'I am with you' means he will not neglect him. But when it is said that someone is 'with the sultan' or 'close to the sultan', it implies high rank and honor. Thus, the two contexts are different and do not conflict; the angelic 'indiyyah indicates honor, while the divine 'indiyyah for believers indicates mercy. The second objection is that the scriptural proof only shows that angels are physically stronger, not necessarily superior in all respects. The author responds by asserting that the argument from strength works only if angels also have perfect knowledge; otherwise, the actions of ignorant beings cannot be used as a proof against knowledgeable ones. Therefore, the angels are superior in knowledge as well, completing the proof of their overall superiority.

Key Terms

شرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'indiyyah in all contexts means the same thing, so the proof for angels is weakened.
Correction: The author shows that 'indiyyah has different meanings: mercy/protection when God is with the servant, and honor when the servant is with God.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the proof from the angels' actions require them to be not only stronger but also more knowledgeable?
A) Because knowledge is more important than strength
B) Because the actions of an ignorant being cannot be used as a proof against a knowledgeable one
C) Because humans are naturally more knowledgeable than angels
D) Because the Quran commands us to seek knowledge

Key Takeaway
The objections against the scriptural proof fail because they confuse different meanings of 'indiyyah and ignore that the proof also implies angels' superiority in knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Angels never cease worshipping Allah despite their immense strength and knowledge. What does your own inconsistency in worship reveal about your heart's attachment to your Creator? Will you commit today to a specific, consistent act of worship that mirrors their constancy?
?
The passage distinguishes between God's protective nearness and the honor of being near to Him. In your daily life, are you merely seeking Allah's protection from harm, or are you actively pursuing the honor of intimate closeness with Him through obedience and knowledge? What one change can you make this week to seek that higher rank?
?

What step will you take today to align your actions with the example of those who are superior in knowledge and strength?

God with You vs. You with God
The author refutes the claim that the verse about angels proves their superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God being with a servant indicates greater glorification than the servant being with God, and how this refutes the claim that the verse about angels proves their superiority.

Core Idea
God's presence with you is more honorable than your presence with Him.

This passage tackles a subtle theological argument about honor. Some might think that the verse 'the angels are with God' proves angels are superior to humans. The author counters with a hadith qudsi: 'I am with the broken-hearted,' showing that God's being with someone is a higher form of glorification than the reverse. Let's examine this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Notice the contrast between the hadith (God with broken-hearted) and the verse (angels with God).
The author uses the phrase 'أكثر إشعاراً بالتعظيم' (more indicative of glorification).
2
Understand the logical contrast
The author argues that God being with the servant is a greater honor than the servant being with God. Ask yourself: why would that be? Because the greater being condescending to the lesser is more exalting.
This refutes the idea that the verse proves angels' superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنكسرة قلوبهم لاجلي ، وهذا أكثر إشعاراً بالتعظيم ، لأن هذا الخبر يدل على أنه سبحانه عند هؤلاء المنكسرين . والآية التي تمسكتم بها : تدل على أن الملائكة عند الله . ولا شك أن كون الله عند العبد ، أدخل في التعظيم من كون العبد عند الله
The broken-hearted are for my sake, and this is more indicative of glorification, because this report indicates that He, exalted, is with these broken-hearted ones. And the verse you have clung to indicates that the angels are with God. And there is no doubt that God's being with the servant is more included in glorification than the servant's being with God.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal against those who use the verse implying angels are with God to argue for their superiority over humans. The author begins by referencing a divine report (hadith qudsi) that God is with the broken-hearted, which is a greater sign of honor—since the majestic one being with the lowly is more exalting than the lowly being with the majestic. He then contrasts this with the verse that states angels are with God. The author argues that God's being with the servant (as in the hadith) is more indicative of glorification than the servant being with God (as in the verse). Thus, the verse does not prove angels' superiority; rather, the hadith shows God's condescension to humans is a greater honor.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the verse 'angels are with God' proves angels are superior to humans.
Correction: The author shows that God's being with the servant (humans) is a greater honor than the servant being with God, so the verse actually supports human dignity, not angelic superiority.

Checkpoint

God's being with you is a greater honor than your being with God.

Refuting the Objection: Angels' Strength Proves Their Superiority
The author presents an objection and gives two answers to refute it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that angels' greater strength does not imply their superiority, using two distinct arguments.

Core Idea
Strength plus knowledge and worship, not strength alone, defines virtue.

The objection claims that being stronger does not make angels better. The author responds with two powerful answers: first, clarifying a hadith about God's protection, and second, arguing that true virtue includes knowledge and power, which angels possess. Let's examine these answers.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first answer
Read the Arabic passage and notice how the objector separates strength from virtue. Then see the first answer interpreting the hadith 'I am with the broken-hearted' as protection, not status.
2
Understand the second answer
The second answer connects strength with knowledge and perfection. Understand why this completes the argument: actions of angels are proofs only if they are superior in knowledge and power.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Consider how the author defends the inference from actions to superiority. The conclusion follows logically: if angels surpass humans in strength and knowledge, they are better.
This ties back to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الاعتراض على الوجه الثاني : فهو أن نقول : لا نزاع في أن الملائكة أشد قدرة وقوة من البشر ، ويكفي في صحة هذا الدليل : هذا القدر من التفاوت ، فإنه يقال : إن الملائكة ، مع شدة قوتهم واستيلائهم على أجرام السموات والأرض ، وأمنهم من الضعف والعجز [ والهرم والمرض وطول أعمارهم (۱) ] لا يتركون العبودية لحظة واحدة. فالبشر مع نهاية ضعفهم [ مع ما يصيبهم من الأمراض والآفات (۲) ] أولى أن لا يتمردوا . فهذا يدل على أن الملائكة أكثر قوة من البشر 1 وهذا القدر كاف في صحة الاستدلال . ولا نزاع في حصول التفاوت في هذا المعنى ] أما لم قلتم : إن ذلك يدل على أن الملائكة أفضل من البشر ؟ والجواب عن الأول : أن نقول : إن قوله : ( أنا عند المنكسرة قلوبهم لأجلي مشعر بأن المراد بتلك العنـديـة : الحفظ والحراسة والرحمة . فإن السلطان إذا قال يا مسكين أنا معك . فهم كل أحد منه : أن المراد أن لا يهمله ولا يضيع مهمه . أما إذا قيل لبعض الأكابر أو العظماء : إنه من المقربين عنـد السلطان . فإنه يفهم منه كمال الدرجة والمنقبة. فعلم أنه لا تعلق لأحد البابين بالآخر والجواب عن السؤال الثاني : إن الاستدلال بأفعال الملائكة إنما يتم إذا قلنا : الملائكة موصوفون بالكمال في القوة والقدرة والعلم . لأنهم لو لم يكونوا أعلم من البشر ، لم يكن فعلهم حجة على البشر لأن فعل الجاهل لا يمكن جعله حجة على العالم . فثبت : أن ذلك الاستدلال ، لا يتم إلا إذا كانت الملائكة زائدين على البشر [ في قوة الإدراك ، وفي قوة العمل . ولا معنى للفضيلة إلا هذا . فإذا ثبت كونهم زائدين على البشر (۱) ] فقد ثبت أنهم أفضل من البشر .
As for the objection concerning the second aspect: it is that we say: there is no dispute that the angels are more powerful and stronger than humans, and this degree of difference is sufficient for the soundness of this proof. For it is said: the angels, despite their intense strength and their domination over the bodies of the heavens and the earth, and their security from weakness and incapacity [and decrepitude and illness and the length of their lives (1)], do not leave worship for a single moment. Humans, with their extreme weakness [along with what befalls them of illnesses and afflictions (2)], are more worthy not to rebel. So this indicates that the angels are stronger than humans. And this degree is sufficient for the soundness of the inference. And there is no dispute about the existence of difference in this meaning. But why do you say: does that indicate that the angels are better than humans? The answer concerning the first: we say: His saying (I am with the broken-hearted for my sake) suggests that what is meant by this 'with-ness' is preservation, protection, and mercy. For if the sultan says 'O poor one, I am with you,' everyone understands from it that what is meant is that he will not neglect him nor waste his affair. But if it is said about some of the elders or great ones: 'He is among those close to the sultan,' then from it is understood complete rank and merit. So it is known that there is no connection between the two aspects. And the answer concerning the second question: that the inference from the actions of the angels is only completed if we say: the angels are described with perfection in strength, power, and knowledge. Because if they were not more knowledgeable than humans, their action would not be a proof against humans, for the action of the ignorant cannot be made a proof against the knowledgeable. So it is established: that this inference is not completed unless the angels are surpassing humans [in the strength of perception and in the strength of action. And there is no meaning of virtue except this. So if it is established that they are surpassing over humans (1)], then it is established that they are better than humans.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation. The objector claims that the argument for angels' superiority based on their strength is insufficient, because being stronger does not necessarily mean being better. The author responds with two answers. First, he clarifies that the hadith 'I am with the broken-hearted' refers to God's protection and mercy, not to a status of honor, so it cannot be used to argue against angels' superiority. Second, he argues that the inference from angels' actions (their constant worship and strength) is valid only because angels are superior in knowledge and power—these are the very meaning of virtue. Therefore, the objection fails, and it is established that angels are indeed superior to humans. The structure is: objection (إعتراض), then two answers (جواب عن الأول and جواب عن السؤال الثاني), then a conclusion (فثبت).

الوجه الثاني
القدرة والقوة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if angels are stronger, they are automatically better, but the objector denies this.
Correction: The author corrects by showing that strength alone is not the basis; it is strength combined with knowledge and worship that constitutes virtue.

Key Takeaway
The author demonstrates that angels' superiority is proven by their combination of strength, knowledge, and constant worship, which constitutes true virtue.

Angels' Perpetual Obedience Makes Them Superior
Argument for angels' superiority through perpetual obedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the perpetual nature of angels' obedience establishes their superiority over humans, based on Qur'anic and prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
Perpetual obedience is the measure of virtue, and angels embody it perfectly.

This lesson examines the second proof for the superiority of angels. The author argues that angels' obedience is more continuous than that of humans, citing a Qur'anic verse that they glorify God night and day without tiring. He then explains why this perpetual worship makes them greater in virtue, and supports his argument with two hadiths that reinforce their elevated status.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to grasp the complete argument.
Notice how the author structures the proof: first establishing perpetuity, then linking it to virtue.
2
Understand the perpetuity claim
Identify the Qur'anic verse (21:20) and the reasoning that even with equal lifespans, angels' obedience is more continuous.
The author uses a conditional argument: even if lifespans were equal, angels win on continuity.
3
Link perpetuity to virtue
See why the author defines virtue as absorption in worship, remembrance, and love of God. Since angels have these more constantly, their virtue is greater.
4
Examine the supporting hadiths
Read the two hadiths: one about the best of servants being long-lived and good-deeded, and another comparing an elder to a prophet. Understand how they imply angels' superiority.
The first hadith directly points to angels, the second uses an analogy.
5
Synthesize the proof
Combine the three elements (Qur'an, reasoning, hadith) to see the full argument for angels' superiority.
This proof is cumulative: each part reinforces the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : طاعات الملائكة أدوم ، فكانت أفضل بيان الأول وهو أنها أدوم : قوله تعالى : ( يسبحون الليل والنهار لا يفترون (۲) ) وعلى هذا التقدير ، فلو كانت أعمارهم مساوية لأعمار البشر ، لكانت طاعتهم أدوم . وأما أنه لا نسبة له ، إلى طاعات البشر . فكيف ، ولا نسبة لعمر كل البشر إلى عمر الملائكة وبيان أنها لما كانت أفضل : لأن الفضيلة ليست إلا في الاستغراق في عبودية الله ، والمواظبة على ذكره ، والابتهاج بمحبته. فإذا كانت هذه المعاني في حقهم أدوم ، وجب أن تكون فضائلهم أكثر. ويؤكده قوله عليه السلام : [ « أفضل العباد من طال عمره ، وحسن عمله والملائكة (۳) ] أطول العباد عمراً وأحسنهم عملاً ، فوجب أن يكونوا أفضل العباد . ولأنه عليه السلام قال : « الشيخ في قومه ، كالنبي في أمته » وهذا يقتضي أن تكون الملائكة بالنسبة إلى البشر ، كالنبي بالنسبة إلى القوم (4) وذلك يوجب فضلهم على البشر .
The second proof: The obedient acts of the angels are more perpetual, so they are better. The explanation of the first [point]—that they are more perpetual—is the saying of the Most High: 'They glorify [Him] night and day, never slackening' (21:20). On this basis, even if their lifespans were equal to the lifespans of humans, their obedience would be more perpetual. How then [can human obedience be compared] when there is no ratio of the lifespan of all humans to the lifespan of angels? And the explanation that they are better: because virtue is only in absorption in the worship of God, persistence in His remembrance, and delight in His love. So if these meanings are more perpetual in their case, then their virtues must be more. And this is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of servants is one whose life is long and whose deeds are good, and the angels are the longest-lived of servants and the best in deeds, so they must be the best of servants.' And because he, peace be upon him, said: 'The elder among his people is like the prophet among his nation.' This requires that the angels, in relation to humans, are like the prophet in relation to the people, and that necessitates their superiority over humans.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a self-contained proof (الحجة الثانية) for the superiority of angels over humans. The proof is twofold. First, the author establishes that angels' obedience is more perpetual (أدوم). He cites the Qur'anic verse that angels glorify God without tiring, and argues that even if their lifespans were equal to humans, their obedience would be more continuous because they never slacken. In reality, angels have much longer lifespans, so the disparity is even greater. Second, he explains why perpetuity makes them better: virtue consists in constant worship, remembrance, and love of God. Since angels have these qualities more continuously, their virtue is greater. He then supports this with two hadiths: one stating that the best of servants are those with long life and good deeds, and since angels have both longest life and best deeds, they are the best; and another comparing the elder among his people to a prophet, implying that angels are to humans as a prophet is to his people—a clear indication of their superiority.

Key Terms
طاعات الملائكة
أدوم
الفضيلة
الاستغراق في عبودية الله
الشيخ في قومه كالنبي في أمته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the quantity of worship does not matter if the quality is the same, but the author assumes equal quality and argues that longer duration increases virtue.
Correction: The passage shows that perpetual obedience, given the same quality, yields greater virtue because virtue consists in continuous devotion.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Third Proof: Angels Are Foremost in All Good Traits
The author presents the third proof for angels' superiority via precedence and constancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof for the superiority of angels: their precedence and unbroken constancy in all good traits from before human creation.

Core Idea
Angels are superior because they pioneered every good trait before humans existed.

In this passage, the author presents the third proof for the superiority of angels over humans. He argues that angels are the foremost in every trait of goodness, having existed long before Adam and having been constant in obedience and knowledge from the very beginning. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to grasp the author's core claim and explanation.
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
Notice the structure: first the claim (they are foremost in good traits, therefore superior), then the explanation (they have been leaders in every religious trait since before Adam).
The phrase 'بيان الأول' signals the beginning of the explanation.
3
Reflect on why precedence plus constancy matters
Ask yourself why simply being first is not enough—the author emphasizes that they were 'مواظبين' (persistent) from the beginning, which adds weight to their superiority.
4
Consider a common misunderstanding
Some might think that temporal precedence alone qualifies superiority. The author addresses this by highlighting the angels' continuous devotion throughout vast ages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إنهم أسبق السابقين في خصال الخير ، فوجب أن يكونوا أفضل من غيرهم . بيان الأول : إنه لا خصلة من خصال الدين ، إلا وهم أئمة متقدمون فيها ، بل هم العامرون لطرق الدين ، لأنهم كانوا موجودين قبل أولاد آدم بل قبل آدم بأعصار عظيمة ، وأدوار متباعدة، وكانوا من أول العمر مواظبين على الطاعات والمعارف
The third proof: They are the foremost of those who precede in the traits of goodness, so it is necessary that they be better than others. The explanation of the first [point]: there is no trait of religion except that they are leaders, advanced in it; rather, they are the ones who populate the paths of religion, because they existed before the children of Adam, even before Adam, for great ages and remote eras, and they were from the beginning of life persistent in acts of obedience and knowledge.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is the third proof (الحجة الثالثة) for the superiority of angels. The author makes two claims: (1) angels are the foremost in all traits of goodness (أسبق السابقين في خصال الخير), and (2) this necessitates their superiority. He explains that there is no religious trait in which angels are not leaders and pioneers. In fact, they are the ones who established and populated the paths of religion, because they existed long before humanity—even before Adam—and from the very beginning of their existence they have been constant in worship and knowledge. This precedence and constancy in good deeds makes them superior to all others.

Proof from Piety: Angels Are More Pious Than Prophets
Proof that angels' complete fear and piety makes them superior to prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the concept of perpetual fear and freedom from slips to argue for the greater piety of angels over prophets and thereby their superiority.

Core Idea
Angels' perpetual fear of God makes their piety more complete than prophets'.

This lesson examines a key argument from the text regarding the superiority of angels over prophets. The author presents a proof based on the nature of piety (taqwa), citing Quranic verses and a hadith to demonstrate that angels, unlike prophets, are free from any form of sin and their fear of God is constant. Understanding this argument helps clarify the theological ranking of these noble beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author's style of argumentation.
The passage is concise and uses Quranic citations.
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
The author first describes angels' perpetual fear and freedom from slips, then contrasts with prophets who had slips. Find these two sections.
Look for 'إنهم مبرأون...' and 'وأما الأنبياء...'.
3
Examine the evidence
Note the Quranic verses cited for angels (يخافون ربهم من فوقهم and وهم من خشيته مشفقون) and the hadith for prophets (ما منا إلا من عصى...).
These are the proofs for each claim.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that since piety is greater in angels, they are more honorable. Trace the logic: greater piety → greater honor (based on Quran 49:13).
This establishes angels' superiority over prophets in this specific aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان الأول: إنهم مبرأون من الزلات، ومن الميل إليها، لأن خوفهم دائم. قال تعالى: {يخافون ربهم من فوقهم} وإشفاقهم دائم. قال تعالى: {وهم من خشيته مشفقون} والخوف والإشفاق ينافيان العزم على المعصية. وأما الأنبياء عليهم السلام: فلم يخل واحد منهم عن نوع زلة. قال عليه السلام: «ما منا إلا من عصى، أو هم بمعصية، غير يحيى بن زكريا» فيثبت: أن تقوى الملائكة أكمل فوجب أن يكونوا أفضل. لقوله تعالى: {إن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم} رتب مزيد الكرامة على مزيد التقوى، فوجب أن يكون مزيد التقوى علة لمزيد الكرامة، فأينها حصل مزيد التقوى، وجب أن يحصل مزيد الكرامة.
Explanation of the first [point]: They (angels) are free from slips and from inclination toward them, because their fear is perpetual. God Almighty said: 'They fear their Lord above them.' And their dread is perpetual. God Almighty said: 'And they are from fear of Him apprehensive.' And fear and dread preclude determination upon disobedience. As for the prophets, peace be upon them, not one of them was free from some kind of slip. He (the Prophet), peace be upon him, said: 'There is none among us except that he sinned or intended a sin, except John son of Zechariah.' So it is established that the piety of angels is more complete, so it necessarily follows that they are superior. For His saying, may He be exalted: 'Indeed the most noble of you in the sight of God is the most pious.' He arranged the increase of honor upon increase of piety, so it necessarily follows that increase of piety is the cause of increase of honor. Therefore, wherever increase of piety is attained, increase of honor must be attained.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (dalil) for the superiority of angels over prophets based on piety (taqwa). The author begins by stating that angels are free from slips (zallat) and from any inclination toward sin because their fear (khawf) and dread (ishfaq) of God are perpetual. He cites two Quranic verses to support this: Quran 16:50 and Quran 21:28. Then he contrasts the prophets: they were not free from slips, as indicated by the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which states that all prophets except John (Yahya) committed sins or intended them. The conclusion: since the piety of angels is more complete, they must be superior. Then he cites Quran 49:13, which states that the most honorable is the most pious. The author argues that God linked honor to piety, so wherever piety is greater, honor must be greater. Thus, angels, having greater piety, are more honorable than prophets.

Key Terms
الزلات (slips)
التقوى (piety)
الخوف (fear)
الإشفاق (dread)
الأنبياء (prophets)
الملائكة (angels)
الكرم (honor)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets' minor sins mean they are less honorable than all angels.
Correction: The passage only argues that angels have greater piety due to perpetual fear, not that prophets are dishonorable. Prophets are still higher than other humans, and their sins are minor and forgiven.

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, why are angels considered more pious than prophets?
A) Because angels never sin, while prophets did sin.
B) Because angels have greater physical power.
C) Because prophets are human.
D) Because angels are created from light.

Key Takeaway
Angels are more pious than prophets because their fear of God is constant, and God's honor is proportioned to piety.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's measure of honor is piety alone, and the angels' fear of Him is perpetual, what does your own intermittent fear of God say about your standing with Him? Will you commit to increasing your awareness of His presence today?
?
The prophets, despite their high rank, had slips. If even they are not perfectly pious, how much more must you guard against complacency in your obedience? What specific sin are you tolerating that you need to uproot now?
?
Angels' fear prevents even the thought of disobedience. When you face a temptation, do you recall that the Lord 'above them' watches you? If not, what practical step can you take to make His awareness real for you in that moment?

Angels' Superiority from Quran 4:172
The author argues from Quran 4:172 that angels are superior because they are mentioned alongside Christ in non-renunciation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Quran 4:172 to argue for the superiority of angels over Christ, and how he refutes an objection about the argument's basis.

Core Idea
If angels are mentioned alongside Christ in non-disdain, their superiority is implied.

This lesson examines a proof from the Quran that the angels brought near are superior to the Messiah. The verse states that neither Christ nor the angels disdain being servants of God. The author argues that the very structure of the verse implies the angels' higher rank. We will explore the reasoning, an objection, and the author's response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the overall argument. Notice the verse quoted and the logical steps.
2
Identify the main proof
Find how the author derives the superiority of angels from the verse. Look at the phrase 'mentioned in the context of argumentation.'
The proof relies on the implication that the argument only works if angels are at least as high as Christ.
3
Understand the objection
The objection suggests the verse might only highlight Christ's weakness compared to angels' power. Read the objection carefully.
The objector uses the phrase 'despite their overpowering dominant power' to argue that Christ's non-disdain is more remarkable.
4
Analyze the author's response
See how the author counters by extending the implication from power to knowledge. Note the analogy about the ignorant and the knowledgeable.
The response shows that the argument's validity requires superiority in both power and knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: {لن يستنكف المسيح أن يكون عبداً لله ولا الملائكة المقربون} فقوله: {ولا الملائكة المقربون} مذكور في معرض الاحتجاج. يعني: أن الملائكة لما لم يستنكفوا، فبأن لا يستنكف المسيح أولى. وهذا الاستدلال إنما يتم إذا كانت الملائكة أفضل من المسيح. فإن قالوا: لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد من هذا أن الملائكة مع قدرهم القاهرة الغالبة لما لم يستنكفوا عن عبادة الله تعالى، فبأن لا يستنكف المسيح ضعفه كان أولى؟ فنقول: هذا كما يدل على أن الملائكة أعلى من البشر في القوة والقدرة، فكذلك يدل على أنهم أعلى من البشر في العلم. وإلا فالاستدلال بفضل الجاهل على العالم لا يصح. فلما صح هذا الاستدلال، وجب كون الملائكة أعلى من المسيح، في كمال القدرة وفي كمال العلم. ولا معنى للفضيلة إلا ذلك.
The sixth proof: His saying, exalted be He: {The Messiah will not disdain to be a servant of God, nor the angels brought near.} So His saying: {nor the angels brought near} is mentioned in the context of argumentation. It means: since the angels did not disdain, then it is more fitting that the Messiah does not disdain. And this argument is only valid if the angels are superior to the Messiah. If they say: Why is it not permissible that the intended [meaning] of this is that the angels, despite their overpowering dominant power, when they did not disdain the worship of God Almighty, then it is more fitting that the Messiah, despite his weakness, does not disdain? Then we say: This, just as it indicates that the angels are higher than humans in power and ability, so too it indicates that they are higher than humans in knowledge. Otherwise, arguing from the merit of an ignorant person over a knowledgeable one is not valid. So when this argument is valid, it necessitates that the angels are higher than the Messiah in perfection of power and in perfection of knowledge. And there is no meaning to virtue except that.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This is a proof from Quran 4:172, which states that neither the Messiah (Jesus) nor the angels brought near disdain being servants of God. The author argues that the mention of angels together with the Messiah in this context implies that angels are superior, because the argument (that they do not disdain) is only effective if angels are at least as high as the Messiah, and the fact that they are mentioned first or equally indicates their higher rank. An objection is raised: perhaps the verse is highlighting that despite the angels' great power, they do not disdain, so it is more noteworthy that the weak Messiah does not disdain. The author answers that this very point also indicates superiority in knowledge, not just power. If the argument were only about power, it would be like comparing an ignorant person to a knowledgeable one, which is invalid. Since the argument is valid, it must also indicate superiority in knowledge, and thus overall virtue.

Key Terms
المسيح (Messiah)
الملائكة المقربون (the angels brought near)
الاستنكاف (disdain)
العبودية (servitude)
القوة (power)
العلم (knowledge)
الفضيلة (virtue)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse only proves that angels and Christ are equal in their servitude to God.
Correction: The author argues that the verse's use as an argument actually implies the superiority of angels, because the reasoning is only valid if angels are at least as high as Christ.

Checkpoint
What is the objection raised against the sixth proof?
A) The verse might only highlight Christ's weakness.
B) The verse is abrogated.
C) The angels are not mentioned.
D) The argument is circular.

Key Takeaway
The author uses Quran 4:172 to argue that angels are superior to Christ in both power and knowledge, which together constitute true virtue.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself disdaining any act of worship, thinking it beneath you or too simple? How does the example of the angels, who despite their immense power do not disdain servitude, challenge your pride?
?
If virtue is defined by power and knowledge combined with humble servitude to God, where do you see a gap in your own life that needs urgent correction?
?
The argument hinges on the logical validity of a Quranic proof. Have you ever dismissed a truth because it required you to accept your own weakness? Will you today embrace the superiority of those who submit completely?
