Satan's Temptation and Angels' Superiority
The author argues from Quran 7:20 that Adam and Eve already believed angels were superior, so Satan used that to tempt them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic verse about Satan's temptation implies that angels are superior to humans, and why this is used as a theological proof.

Core Idea
Satan's argument only works if Adam already believed angels are superior.

This lesson examines a brief but powerful proof from the Qur'an. Allah narrates Satan's words to Adam and Eve, tempting them to eat from the forbidden tree by claiming that God only forbade it to prevent them from becoming angels. The author argues that this deception could only succeed if Adam and Eve already held the belief that angels are superior to humans. Thus, the verse itself becomes evidence for the superiority of angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its context
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Satan's statement is a direct quote from the Qur'an.
The verse is Surah Al-A'raf (7:20).
2
Analyze the author's reasoning
The author points out that Satan's temptation relies on a shared belief. Identify that shared belief: angels are superior to humans.
If Adam and Eve did not believe angels were better, Satan's offer would not be tempting.
3
Reflect on the implication about angels
Consider why this argument is used as a proof for angels' superiority. It shows that even the first humans knew this truth.
This is a sam'iyyat argument, based on revealed text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى حكاية عن إبليس: {ما نهاكما ربكما عن هذه الشجرة إلا أن تكونا ملكين} ولو لم يكن متقرراً عند آدم وحواء أن الملك أفضل من البشر، وإلا لما قدر إبليس أن يغرهما بهذا الكلام.
The seventh proof: His saying, exalted be He, relating from Iblis: {He said: 'Your Lord did not forbid you this tree except that you become angels.'} And if it were not established in the minds of Adam and Eve that the angel is superior to the human, then Iblis would not have been able to deceive them with this speech.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This is a brief argument from Quran 7:20. Satan (Iblis) tempted Adam and Eve by saying that God only forbade the tree to prevent them from becoming angels. The author argues that this temptation would only be effective if Adam and Eve already held the belief that angels are superior to humans. Thus, the verse implies that the superiority of angels is a known fact, even among the first humans.

Key Terms
إبليس (Iblis/Satan)
آدم (Adam)
حواء (Eve)
الملك (angel)
الغُرور (deception)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Satan's statement is a lie and has no theological value.
Correction: The author uses the fact that Adam and Eve believed Satan's claim as evidence that they already considered angels superior.

Checkpoint
Why does the author use Satan's statement as a proof?
A) Because it shows that angels are better than humans.
B) Because it proves Satan is a liar.
C) Because it shows the tree was forbidden.
D) Because it proves Adam's disobedience.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic account of Satan's temptation reveals that Adam and Eve inherently recognized the superiority of angels over humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you, like Adam and Eve, hold an unconscious belief that some creation (angels, scholars, or even peers) is more beloved or closer to Allah than you are? How does that belief affect your actions and reliance on Allah? What step can you take today to internalize your own honor as a human being chosen by Allah?
?
Think of a temptation you have experienced. Did it succeed because it tapped into a hidden insecurity or a belief that you were 'less than'? How would understanding that this doubt is a tool of Satan, as in this lesson, change your response next time?
?
Are you willing to examine your heart for any false belief that makes you susceptible to deception—such as thinking you are not good enough for Allah's mercy? What one specific false belief will you actively work to replace with the truth taught in this lesson this week?
